From the Director’s Desk
In the heart of the Thar Desert, IIT Jodhpur stands as a testament to the harmonious coexistence of 
technology and nature, each enriching the other. Our 852-acre campus is more than just a collection of 
buildings; it is a thriving ecosystem, home to a diverse array of flora and fauna. Designed with foresight and 
vision, 
it 
embodies 
sustainability 
through 
zero 
wastewater 
discharge, 
rainwater 
harvesting, 
decentralised waste treatment systems, and climate-responsive features such as berms that deflect 
sandstorms and thermally insulated walls that conserve energy.
The year 2024-25 has been transformative, marked by innovation, academic reform, research excellence, and 
responsible growth, all under the guiding vision of ‘IIT Jodhpur 5.0 – Scaling Up and Shaping the Future 
(2024-29).’ This strategic framework reaffirms our commitment to advancing education, research, 
entrepreneurship, and social responsibility, with inclusivity and sustainability at its core. This year also marked a 
significant upgradation and expansion in infrastructure. Supported by a ₹6 72-crore HEFA loan, we embarked on 
the Phase 3B development of our campus, which features new lecture halls and academic blocks, thematic 
research laboratories in various areas, including quantum and photonics, expanded housing and dining facilities, 
new hostels, a visitor’s hostel, and a technology park. The inauguration of our new Lecture Hall Complex by 
Hon’ble Speaker Shri Om Birla was a proud milestone, signalling the Institute’s steady rise as a hub of 
knowledge creation.
Our academic ecosystem continues to evolve through bold reforms and the introduction of new 
educational programs. We launched the School of Design, the Rishabh Centre for Clean Energy, the 
Manekshaw Centre for National Security Studies, and the MedTech Centre. These initiatives 
complement joint centres with NLU Jodhpur, ARIES Nainital, and AIIMS Jodhpur, expanding an 
interdisciplinary landscape that connects engineering, design, astronomy, science, health, and policy.
Curriculum innovations have consistently kept pace with national priorities and emerging technologies. New 
offerings in drone and anti-drone technology, intelligent systems, bridge engineering and smart 
product design broaden the experiential learning and industry relevance. In alignment with NEP 2020 
and our belief that language should never be a barrier to learning or belonging, IIT Jodhpur 
introduced first-year teaching in the Matribhasha (native language) - one of the first initiatives of its kind in 
the IIT system.

Several foundational courses are now being offered bilingually, with lectures delivered in English and 
Hindi for those who opt for the latter. The results are heartwarming: students who might otherwise feel 
hesitant in an English-only classroom are more engaged, confident, and participative. This approach has 
eased the transition into the rigour of IIT life, strengthened peer interaction, and deepened conceptual 
understanding by allowing students to think and express themselves in the language they are comfortable with. 
In the same spirit of inclusive and future-ready education, we launched the Integrated Teacher 
Education Programme (ITEP) - a four-year program to develop school teachers who can blend scientific 
inquiry, digital innovation, and novel pedagogy. We also introduced the Director’s Fellowship to support early 
PhD completion, enabled direct PhD admissions for top NIT graduates, and revamped postgraduate 
programs to strengthen their research orientation. Our placement performance remained robust, with over 
415 job offers comprising 85% of all students enrolled for placement, including 70+ from Fortune 500 
companies and 20+ international offers.
On the research front, IIT Jodhpur recorded more than 100% year-on-year growth in project registrations. 
Flagship 
initiatives 
launched 
or 
accelerated 
this 
year 
include 
the 
DST-supported 
Jodhpur 
Hydrogen Valley Innovation Cluster, the IITJ-JJM Centre for Sustainable Drinking Water, the 
DRDO–Industry–Academia Centre of Excellence for defence technologies, the AyurTech Centre of 
Excellence supported by the 
Ministry 
of 
AYUSH, 
and 
the 
Deep-Tech 
Biodesign 
Centre 
for 
MedTech. Together, these ventures illustrate the breadth of IIT Jodhpur’s contribution - from clean 
energy and water security to national defence and the blending of ancient health wisdom with 
cutting-edge 
technology. 
Our 
Section-8 innovation entities - iHub Drishti, the AIoT Innovation 
Hub, IITJ Research Park, and the Technology Innovation and Startup Centre (TISC) continued to 
catalyse entrepreneurship and product development, supporting startups through the PRAYAS and Seed 
Support schemes.
Equally important has been the strengthening of the welfare of our campus community. A new 
Primary Health 
Centre 
and 
AMRIT 
Pharmacy, 
expanded 
transport 
services, 
and 
enhanced 
amenities - encompassing housing, dining, and vibrant community spaces - have significantly improved the 
quality of life for all members of the IIT Jodhpur community. Faculty affairs have been streamlined and 
energised. Birsa Munda Postdoctoral Fellowship is attracting outstanding young researchers, while 
alumni engagement has grown stronger, with our graduates contributing across various sectors and 
geographies. Our international footprint has also significantly expanded. IIT Jodhpur signed several 
MoUs with international universities. They launched direct admission pathways for top international 
students to IIT Jodhpur, reinforcing our identity as a global centre for technology, innovation, and 
education, offering students and faculty diverse opportunities for exchange, joint research, and co-
creation of technology.
Sustainability 
remains 
at 
the 
core 
of 
our 
development 
philosophy. 
Through 
the 
Centre 
for 
Emerging Technologies for Sustainable Development (CETSD), the Green Cell, and the Office of 
Infrastructure Engineering, we are advancing towards a net-zero, green campus. Initiatives like “Ek Ped Maa 
ke Naam” and the “Swachhata Hi Sewa” campaign, as well as IoT-enabled waste-management systems, 
are shaping the habits of the IIT Jodhpur community as much as the infrastructure. Our outreach 
programs engage the wider community, fostering a culture of clean, green, and responsible living on our 
beautiful campus. Our faculty and students continue to bring laurels through their research, awards, 
and innovations. With a sustained emphasis on talent development, interdisciplinary learning, and social 
engagement, IIT Jodhpur is positioned as a vital contributor to a Viksit Bharat by 2047.
Looking ahead, our ambitions are no longer confined to a single campus. The IIT J3 vision at 
Jodhpur, Jaipur, and Jaisalmer is taking shape, each site uniquely positioned to advance our mission. 
Jodhpur will continue to anchor technology and sustainability, while Jaipur will catalyse AI, design, 
management, and incubation. Jaisalmer will emerge as a hub for desert ecology, astrophysics, and 
national security. Together, these nodes will form a connected IIT ecosystem in Rajasthan, deeply rooted in 
India’s cultural and ecological contexts while engaging global challenges and opportunities. As we move 
forward, IIT Jodhpur remains steadfast in its pursuit of excellence, driven by the collective passion 
and dedication of our faculty, staff, students, alumni, and partners. Together, we will continue to 
shape a future where science, technology, and human values unite to build a sustainable, empowered and 
strong Bharat.
Avinash Kumar Agarwal, Director, IIT Jodhpur

DEPARTMENT OF BIOSCIENCE & BIOENGINEERING (BSBE)
VIision: 
To excel in developing bioengineering solutions for healthcare, food, energy & environment, through 
multidisciplinary research and teaching/learning ecosystem.
Mission
Curriculum and Pedagogy: Generation of competent human resources capable of addressing the fast–
evolving challenges in the domain of bioscience and bioengineering pertinent to human life by implementing a 
future centric, broad-based curriculum design based on technology foresight and trans-disciplinary academic 
collaborations.
Research: To conduct high quality basic and translational research with primary focus in the areas of healthcare, 
food, energy, and environment aiming to seek technological solutions for societal needs.
Innovation: Build an innovation ecosystem by promoting original and creative ideas from faculty & students for 
the development of sustainable bioengineering solutions in identified thrust areas. Revenue generation and 
Infrastructure: To excel in application-oriented research domains such as drug 
design, 
biosensors, 
molecular 
modelling 
and simulation, 
protein 
engineering, 
tissue 
engineering and genetically engineered 
microbes by leveraging academic and industrial fraternities for revenue generation and strengthening infrastructure.

New Laboratory Facilities:
1.
Image enabled Fluorescence Activated Cell Sorting (FACs)
facility: The recently established FACS facility enables different
cellular parameters analyses along with cell sorting. This facility
allow validating the cells being sorted by providing a virtual
image expressing unique combinations of molecular markers.
2.
Animal House Facility: Our faculty members have contributed to 
the establishment and functionalization of a modern animal 
house, which would enable testing novel drugs, tissue implants, 
medical devices, food and nutraceutical testing, material testing, 
and any other customized experiments
3.
Plant Functional Genomics Facility: a repository of 300 
Arabidopsis thaliana worldwide ecotypes and over 200 knockout 
lines established, enabling research on abiotic stress tolerance 
genes.
4.
Next Generation sequencing Core Facility: Illumina Nextseq 2000 
and Seqstudio 8 Flex platforms installed and fully functional at 
TISC. This facility will enable genomic and transcriptomic 
sequencing for precision medicine.

Events Organized:
1.
The five day intensive workshop “Ayurtech for precision Tech” was conducted for MD Ayurveda graduates 
by BSBE Faculties in collaboration with national council. It aimed to advance Ayurtech Training, develop 
research protocols, and integrate AI and genomics for personlised Ayurveda, fostering a Tech driven, 
evidence based future in integrative medicine.
2.
The Three day molecular motors, transport, and tracks (M2T2-2025) conference 17 -19 February 2025, 
organized by Dr. Priyanka Singh at IIT Jodhpur brought together researchers, clinicians and Industry leaders 
took explore cutting edge advances in molecular motors and membrane, trafficking.
3.
Two weeks hands-on course on Antibiotic Discovery from Soil bacteria coordinated by the Dr. Shankar 
Monoharan to combat anti-microbial resistance.
4.
Three days hands-on workshop on spectral flow cytometry and image enabled cell sorting.

DEPARTMENT OF CHEMICAL ENGINEERING
Established in 2020, the Department of Chemical Engineering at IIT Jodhpur strives to become a pioneer in 
modern approaches to chemical engineering education, in accordance with the national education policy NEP2020. 
The program involves traditional courses, emerging areas and specializations such as process engineering 
intelligence, molecular engineering and sustainability. With Industry 4.0 transforming the chemical industry, 
AI and IoT for chemical engineering forms an integral part of the curriculum. Our programs offer a structured 
foundation to foster scientific mind-set, independent thought, and the development of skills for scientific 
entrepreneurship that:
•
Aim to excel in process engineering, molecular engineering, and sustainability
•
Drive research to convert molecular knowledge into sustainable products and processes
•
Build a research culture that tackles environmental and societal issues through scientific responsibility
•
Foster a net-positive department through start-ups, consultancy, technology transfer, and industry-academia
partnerships
Vision:
“To become a globally recognized department of chemical engineering through its contribution in emerging 
and demand-driven areas with a multidisciplinary approach.”
Faculty Awards and Achievements during 2024-2025:
Scholar-in-Residence:
Professor Ashutosh Sharma is an institute and INAE Visvesvarya Chair Professor in the Department 
of Chemical Engineering, Indian Institute of Technology Kanpur. His research interests include functional and 
nano-materials, carbon micro/nanostructures and composites, interfacial and colloidal interactions, multiscale 
MEMS/NEMS and microfluidic systems, soft interfaces and soft nanofabrication. He is a very decorated 
scientist who is conferred with several awards and fellowships including the Infosys prize, Bhatanagar 
award, J. C. Bose fellowship and elected fellowships of all national academies of India.

DEPARTMENT OF CHEMISTRY
Vision
To achieve academic excellence and be acknowledged for high quality fundamental, sustainable, and 
translational research in chemical sciences and allied research areas meeting global standards
Mission
•
Create a knowledge platform to educate and prepare competitive and professional graduates with an 
innovative and intellectually stimulating mind.
•
Reach out to neighboring institutes for promoting our programs and attract talented young minds to enroll 
in the department’s programs.
•
Support technology transfer from basic science research to realize materials from molecules.
•
Collaborate and build proactive partnership with world renowned educational institutes and industry.
•
Promote interdisciplinary research projects targeting national missions and encourage research scholars to 
take up interdisciplinary projects for thesis work.
•
Participating in the interdisciplinary research platforms in the Institute wherein chemical sciences can 
potentially contribute.
•
Promote scientific communication and outreach to share recent advances in chemical sciences to the general 
community targeting young minds.
Goal
•
Enhance the employability quotient of graduates and prepare them for higher education
•
Build state-of-the-art research facilities to support innovation in research
•
Promote collaborative research with academia and industry targeting sustainable technologies
•
Participate in joint research projects at the national and international level
Programs
•
Undergraduate Program:
▪
BS with Specialization in Chemistry (An engineering linked four-year Program with specialization)
▪
BSc. BEd. Program: The Institute has launched a four-year ITEP program, in which Chemistry major
 is also a part of it.
•
Postgraduate Program:
▪
M.Sc. in Chemistry (A two-year program with year-long project exposure)
▪
M.Sc.-M.Tech. (A four-years program with M.Sc. in Chemistry and M.Tech. in Materials Engineering)
▪
Ph.D. (An extensive curriculum to engage motivated students in fundamental and applied areas of 
chemistry)

ChemMeet
The Department of Chemistry organized its first in-house symposium, "ChemMeet-2024," on 5th October 
2024. The program started at 9 AM in the morning and continued up to 6 PM in the evening. The aim 
of this one-day symposium was to bring together all the departmental faculties and students and make 
each stakeholder acquainted with the cutting-edge, fundamental, and interdisciplinary research programs 
ongoing in the department. This event comprised invited lectures by departmental faculty members and 
Ph.D. students. In addition, there was a poster session by the students.

Empowering the Next Generation of Researchers! On January 27, 2025, IIT Jodhpur, in collaboration with the 
American Chemical Society (ACS), hosted Navigating PhD and Beyond—a dynamic event designed to equip 
young researchers with the essential skills, perspectives, and strategies to excel in academia and industry. The 
event featured insightful sessions by distinguished experts, including Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal (Director, IIT 
Jodhpur), Prof. Ashutosh Sharma, Scholar in Residence and President, INSA, Dr. Deeksha Gupta (ACS), Dr. Anand 
Madhukar (TERI SAS), and Dr. Ajay Jha (ACS). Key takeaways: Importance of sustainability in research Mastering 
the art of scientific communication Navigating career pathways & making the most of a PhD A day filled with 
knowledge-sharing, networking, and inspiration, this event reaffirmed the commitment to fostering a robust 
research ecosystem
Navigating PhD and Beyond

Department of Civil & Infrastructure Engineering

•
Develop unique courses in the field of Civil and Infrastructure Engineering through advanced UG and PG 
programs with a multidisciplinary perspective.
•
Establish high-quality teaching and research facilities in the areas of smart, resilient, and sustainable 
infrastructure engineering to foster the needs of society.
•
Promote consilient research through application of AI/ML, cyber-physical systems, digital twin and 
advanced visualization in the areas of Energy, Environment, Transportation, and Construction.
•
Promote innovative and entrepreneurial activities through intellectual property generation and transfer.
•
Nurture the potential of students to become future leaders in the Civil Engineering industry for 
leadership achievements, scientific breakthroughs and social welfare.

DEPARTMENT OF CIVIL & INFRASTRUCTURE ENGINEERING
The Department of Civil and Infrastructure Engineering at IIT Jodhpur was established in January 2020 and 
launched its academic programs for the 2020-2021 year. Responding to the rapid urbanization and rising 
demand for intelligent infrastructure, the department offers innovative programs that blend traditional 
civil engineering with advanced technologies like artificial intelligence, cyber-physical systems, and digital 
twins. Key focus areas include Energy and Environment, Building Sciences, Safety, and Services, 
Applications of AI, IoT, and CPS in Civil and Infrastructure Engineering, Smart and Integrated 
Infrastructure, 
Urban 
Architecture 
and 
Planning, 
Construction 
Technology 
and 
Management, 
Transportation 
Engineering, 
Structural 
Engineering, 
Geotechnical 
Engineering, 
Water 
resources 
Engineering, and Engineering Geology. The department aims to train graduates who are well-
versed in multidisciplinary approaches and emerging technologies for effective infrastructure design and 
management. The department is guided by following vision and mission:
Academic Programmes

•

Research Highlights
•
Techno-economic analysis of solar-powered green hydrogen production in Rajasthan and its 
large-scale underground storage in South Asia’s sedimentary basins.
•
Physical and chemical characterization of atmospheric aerosols through laboratory and field 
experiments using various 
state-of-the-art 
and 
advanced 
analytical 
techniques 
essential 
to 
understand their origin, fate and environmental and health impacts. The group performs offline 
and online (real-time) measurements of gas and particles to identify their sources and investigate 
long-term changes in emissions and effectiveness of regulatory measures.
•
Driving simulator development, dynamic traffic assignment for multi-vehicle class traffic lacking lane 
discipline, travel behaviour and public transit studies, environment Impact on ridership, and accident 
risk prediction.
•
Steel structure testing and design, high-strength steel, tubular and thin-walled structures, concrete-filled 
steel tubes, fire-resistant structural design, steel corrosion and retrofitting, and sustainable infrastructure.

•
Performance-based structural fire engineering, advanced computational modeling of steel and 
composite structures, fatigue and fracture mechanics, hybrid structural systems, seismic performance of steel 
structures, and durability assessment of infrastructure materials.
•
Design and behavior of metamaterials with tailored properties, such as phononic band gaps and negative 
Poisson's ratios, enabling control over wave transmission and vibration attenuation. The applications 
include advanced vibration isolation systems, energy absorption devices, and innovative materials for 
structural engineering applications.
•
Seismic stability of foundations for critical infrastructure through physical and numerical modelling 
techniques. Sand dune erosion in Thar Desert along with sustainable measures for mitigation the same 
are also being investigated. Additional research focuses on waste management and efficient 
valorization for engineering applications.
•
Resilient and sustainable infrastructure with special emphasis on sustainable building materials. This work 
focuses on various aspects of cement and concrete science, ranging from the mechanics of cement 
hydration to the durability issues in concrete.
•
Monitoring and risk assessment of environmental contaminants and treatment of municipal and 
industrial wastewater using innovative biological and hybrid treatment technologies.
•
Water quality, recovery and remediation, solute and colloid fate and transport, environmental applications 
and implications of nanotechnology.

Department of Computer Science & Engineering

DEPARTMENT OF COMPUTER SCIENCE & ENGINEERING
The Department of Computer Science and Engineering is deeply rooted in excellence and innovation, we are committed 
to pushing the frontiers of knowledge and technology. Our focus remains on developing solutions that have a profound 
impact on society. Whether it's through pioneering research in artificial intelligence, advancing the frontiers of data 
science, or exploring new computational paradigms.
The faculty members work in different core and allied areas of computer science including theoretical computer science, 
high performance computing, networking, software, Artificial Intelligence, Machine Learning, and cyber-physical 
system security. Our faculty, students, and researchers are engaged in cutting-edge research and interdisciplinary 
collaborations, addressing some of the most pressing challenges of our time.The research activities of the department 
are supported by agencies such as the Department of Science and Technology, Ministry of Electronics and Information 
Technology, and Ministry of Home Affairs. The department works closely with industry leaders like Microsoft, Meta, 
Accenture, Intel, and TCS, and academic and research collaborators like IIT Delhi, IIT Kanpur, IIT Bombay, and AIIMS 
Jodhpur.
The faculty members have several international collaborations with universities like University of Texas A&M at 
Kingsville and SUNY at Buffalo. The department is steadily striving towards excellence in both academics, research and 
service to the community with active participation from faculty, staff and students.
•
Sankar Kumar Pal

Department of Electrical Engineering

DEPARTMENT OF ELECTRICAL ENGINEERING
The Department of Electrical Engineering was initially started in 2009 as the Centre for Information and Communication 
Technologies (ICT), and later developed into a full-fledged Department in 2015. As of 2025, the Department offers a 
wide range of degree programs at UG, Masters, Dual-degree, and Doctoral levels, with curricula that cater to the needs 
of next-generation engineers and researchers. The Department leverages technology-enhanced learning and innovative 
teaching pedagogies to impart
quality engineering education in the increasingly digital world. With 38 faculty members working in diverse areas of 
electrical engineering, the Department has an h-index of 54 with over 1000 publications and numerous patents. With 
new workforce-ready degree programs, and cutting-edge curriculum handcrafted to meet the requirements of the 
rapidly evolving industry, the Department collaborates with organizations around the world, and produces graduates 
who are well-equipped to tackle complex challenges and make a meaningful impact in their careers. The Department 
has state-of-the-art research infrastructure and actively focuses on emerging technology tracks in the areas of electrical 
engineering such as 5G & Beyond Communication, Signal Processing & Interpretation, Cyber Physical Systems, 
Nanoelectronics & Integrated Circuits, Smart Grid, Embedded Computing & SoC, and Artificial Intelligence of Things
Academic Programmes:
The Department offers a range of degree programs with a flexible and broad-based curriculum. These programs are as 
follows:
Undergraduate Program
•
BTech in Electrical Engineering (4 Years)
•
BTech with Specialization (4 Years) in
•
Cyber Physical Systems, Artificial Intelligence of Things (AIoT), Communication Engineering
•
Intelligent Communication and Networking, VLSI Systems, Nano and Flexible Electronics
•
Visual Computing, Smart Grid, Engineering Innovation
•
BTech with Minor (4 Years)
•
BTech–MTech Dual-degree (5 Years)
•
BTech–MBA Dual-degree (5 Years)
Postgraduate Programs:
•
MTech (Intelligent Communication Systems)
•
MTech (Cyber Physical Systems)
•
MTech (Sensors and Internet of Things)
•
MTech (Intelligent VLSI Systems)
•
MTech-PhD Dual Degree (Intelligent Communication Systems)

Thematic/Thrust Research Areas:
The research areas pursued by faculty members of the Department of Electrical Engineering broadly covers the following 
areas of conventional electrical engineering: Communication Engineering, RF, Microwave and Photonics, Signal 
Processing, Microelectronics and VLSI, Control Systems, Power Engineering & Computing Systems. The Department has 
also identified six technology tracks of emerging technologies in these areas:
•
5G & Beyond Communication
•
Signal Processing & Interpretation
•
Cyber-Physical Systems
•
Nano electronics & Integrated Circuits
Laboratories
The Department of Electrical Engineering hosts state-of-the-art research facilities with world-class infrastructure and 
computational facilities.
•
Cyber Physical System Modelling Laboratory
•
Control and Computing Laboratory
•
Device Modeling & Mems Simulation Laboratory
•
Basic Electrical & Electronics Lab
•
Electronic Circuit Simulation and VLSI Systems Lab
•
Electrical Machines Lab
•
Image Processing and Computer Vision Lab
•
Internet of Things (IoT) Laboratory
•
Lightwave Technology Laboratory

Research Highlights:
•
Cyber Security for Power System Protection Relays: This project focuses on safeguarding power system relays
against cyber threats. It aims to enhance the reliability and security of critical grid infrastructure.
•
AIOT Based Water Quality Monitoring : Combines Artificial Intelligence and IoT for real-time water quality
assessment. The system ensures safe water usage through continuous environmental sensing.
•
Transforming Health Care through Technology Innovation : Aims to revolutionize healthcare by integrating
advanced technologies in diagnostics and treatment. It supports innovation in digital and remote health services.
•
Reproductive Child Health Care (ई-ASHA) : Develops a digital platform to monitor maternal and child health in
rural regions. It promotes better health outcomes through timely interventions and awareness.
•
Development of Low-Cost Mobile Robots : Designs affordable mobile robots for academic, industrial, and service
applications. Focus is on enhancing accessibility and automation in low-resource settings.
•
Enabling Technologies for Intelligent Wireless Sensor Network for Health Monitoring : Creates smart sensor
networks for continuous patient health monitoring. Aims to improve remote diagnostics and reduce hospitalization
needs.
•
Smart Health Solution for Rapid Mass Diagnosis for COVID-19 : Develops scalable diagnostic tools for quick
COVID-19 detection. Ensures rapid screening and decision-making in public health scenarios.
•
AI-driven Digital Twin Technology for Optimal Condition Monitoring and Energy Management of Solar Power
Plants : Uses AI-enabled digital twins for predictive maintenance and energy optimization. Helps increase the
efficiency and lifespan of solar power systems.
•
Exploring ‘Smart’ Pedagogy through the End-to-End Development of a Technology-Enhanced Learning (TEL)
System : Builds a smart learning ecosystem using modern pedagogy and digital tools. Enhances student engagement
and adaptive learning experiences.
•
An Endoscopic Camera System : Develops a compact and affordable camera system for minimally invasive surgery.
Aims to improve accessibility to endoscopic procedures in remote areas.
•
Establishment of AI-Based Platform to Monitor and Identify Smell, Taste and Key COVID-19 Therapeutic Hotspots
: Utilizes AI and sensing technologies to detect chemical cues linked to COVID-19. Helps identify potential hotspots
and improve public health response.
•
Human Perception Driven On-Chip Compression for Power Efficient CMOS Image Sensors : Implements visual
models to compress image data efficiently on-chip. Reduces power consumption in portable and embedded imaging
devices.
•
Development of OECT Sensor for Lung Cancer Biomarkers Detection : Develops a highly sensitive sensor using
OECT technology. Focuses on non-invasive early detection of lung cancer biomarkers.
•
Telepresence and Teleaction System for Robot Assisted Dentistry : Creates a remotely operable robotic system for
dental care. Enables precision procedures with real-time control and feedback.
•
Haptics Based Medical Simulator for Abdomen Palpation and Pulse Behavior : Builds a haptic simulator for medical
training in abdominal examination. Enhances skill development in clinical palpation and diagnostics

•
Electronic Nose System Based Asthma Detection through Exhaled Breath : Develops a sensor-based system to detect
asthma through breath analysis. Aims to provide non-invasive, early diagnosis tools.
•
Point of Use and In-Line Coliforms Sensors for Smart Water Management : Designs sensors for immediate detection
of bacterial contamination in water. Supports real-time quality monitoring in water distribution systems.
•
Fabrication and Characterization of Sensors Towards Electronic Nose Applications : Investigates sensor materials
and designs for artificial olfaction systems. Focuses on improving sensitivity and selectivity of electronic noses.
•
Nanostructured Metal Oxides for Efficient Detection of Breast Cancer : Uses nanostructured materials for
high-performance cancer biomarker detection. Enables early, non-invasive diagnosis of breast cancer.
•
Development of Porous Silicon Based Biosensor Device for Detection of E. Coli Bacterium for Safe Drinking Water :
Creates a biosensor using porous silicon to detect E. Coli in water. Aims to enhance safety in drinking water through
fast microbial detection.
•
Flexible Sensing Device for Detection of E. Coli in Water : Develops bendable and lightweight sensors for bacterial
detection. Supports portable and on-site water quality assessment.
•
Imprinted Polymers for Sensing and Removal of Selected Antibiotic and Pesticide Residue : Designs molecularly
imprinted polymers for dual sensing and removal applications. Targets environmental safety from chemical
residues.
•
Development of Biodegradable Electronic Devices for Sustainable ICT : Focuses on creating eco-friendly electronics
using biodegradable components. Aims to reduce electronic waste and support sustainable tech.
•
Multifunctional Flexible Devices for Eco-Sustainable E-Textile Applications : Designs flexible, wearable electronics
for environmental and health monitoring. Promotes sustainability in smart textile development.
•
Feasibility Study of Organic Field Effect Transistors for Radiation Detection (RAD-OFETs) : Explores organic
transistors as cost-effective radiation sensors. Targets applications in medical imaging and nuclear safety monitoring.
New Laboratory:
•
Power Engineering Lab: Numerical distance relay, differential Protection relay, motor protection relay, Directional
Overcurrent Relay and generator protection relay setups are developed for the power engineering course
•
Transportation Electrification lab (T.E.L): Wireless Chargers for EVs and UAVs, Battery management system,
actuators for automotive application
•
Energy Management and Microgrid Laboratory (EMML): Lab scale Microgrid setup
•
G Lab: Under the Department of Telecommunications’ initiative to establish 5G Use Case Labs across academic
institutions, a 5G Lab has been installed at IIT Jodhpur. This initiative aims to promote cutting-edge research,
innovation, and the development of real-world applications leveraging 5G technology.As an Institute of National
Importance, IIT Jodhpur is fully committed to supporting this visionary program. The 5G Lab is being actively
integrated into both academic and research activities, providing students, researchers, and faculty with hands-on
access to advanced 5G infrastructure.

Department of Mathematics

DEPARTMENT OF MATHEMATICS
Mathematics, being the basis of many disciplines, is a subject that evolves with time and creates new theories to solve 
real-world challenging problems. The department has been taking a leading role in developing new methods to model 
such situations that can be used in diverse areas of computer science, engineering, and basic sciences. We are excited to 
offer high-quality programs at undergraduate level and postgraduate level for students who wish to apply math to science 
or engineering such as a four-year B.Sc-B.Ed program in Mathematics, two-year M.Sc. program in Mathematics, a 
four-year M.Sc-M.Tech. program in Mathematics-Data and Computational Sciences, a two year M.Tech program in Data 
and Computational Sciences. We also offer a Ph.D. degree program in different areas of mathematics to earn a deeper 
understanding of pure mathematics, applied mathematics and data & computational sciences. The department has faculty 
with research interests in the areas of Algebra, Lie Groups and its Applications, Cryptography and Network Security, 
Mathematical Physics, Fluid Dynamics, Scientific Computations, Optimization, Frame Theory, Reinforcement learning, 
Physics Informed Neural Networks, Numerical Analysis, Partial Differential Equations, Topological Dynamics, Low 
Dimensional Chaos, Dynamical Systems, Renormalization Theory, Wavelet Analysis, Fractional Transform Theory, Image 
Processing, Financial Risk Analysis, Categorical Data Analysis, Reliability Theory and Applied Probability, Differential 
Geometry, Riemannian Geometry, Complex Geometry, Contact Geometry, etc. The Department of Mathematics has been 
located in a semi-permanent building, since December 2022, which is situated behind the Department of physics.

Faculty Awards and Achievements during 2024-2025
Student's Achievements during 2024-2025
Research Highlights:
•
Abhishek Sarkar: My research interests primarily focus on nonlinear analysis and partial differential equations (PDEs),
particularly on local and nonlocal elliptic problems. My current areas of interest includes: Elliptic PDEs, Nonlocal
Operators, Singular and Degenerate Equations, Hardy-Rellich-type Inequalities and Eigenvalue Problems, Multiplicity
Results and Variational Methods, and Moser-Trudinger Type Inequalities. My research integrates deep functional
analysis with advanced techniques from nonlinear differential equations, enabling me to address complex analytical
problems in mathematical physics and geometry.
•
Bimal Mandal: I am working in the area of cryptographic Boolean functions and cryptanalysis of block and stream
ciphers. My research contributes to the analysis and characterization of the basic building of symmetric key
cryptosystems.
•
Dilpeet Kaur: The broad area of research interest is group theory and its applications in other areas related to algebra.
More specifically, I am interested in studying conjugacy classes and representations of finite groups, and connections
between properties of conjugacy classes and properties of irreducible representations. I also work in the area of quandles
and quandle rings, we used group theoretic results to understand the enumeration of some classes of quandles.
•
Gaurav Bhatnagar: I primarily work in the areas of wavelet and fractional transform analysis, of which I am interested
in both pure and applied aspects. On the pure aspect, I am interested in proposing the new construction process for
wavelets and fractional transform analysis. On the applied aspect, my broad interest lies in the application of my
expertise in computer science, particularly, Information security, Biometrics, Information Fusion, Image Segmentation
and Image Completion.
•
Kirankumar R. Hiremath: Our research lies at the intersection of applied mathematics and physics, addressing complex,
real-world problems through a powerful blend of mathematical modeling, simulation, and applied functional analysis.
We focus on nonlinear and quantum-inspired systems, with key contributions in areas such as light propagation in bent
waveguides, the nonlinear dynamics of coupled Josephson junctions, and the development of physics-informed neural
networks to discover modes in complex waveguide structures. By fusing rigorous mathematics with emerging
technologies, our work advances fundamental understanding while opening new avenues for transformative
applications in photonics, quantum computing, and large-scale optimization.
•
Kuntal Som: I broadly work on mathematical optimization. In particular I work on set-valued optimization, bilevel
programming and nonsmooth analysis applicable to optimization.
•
Md Abu Talhamainuddin Ansary: I am working in the area of multi-objective optimization problems. Currently I am
developing some efficient numerical techniques for different type nonlinear multi-objective optimization problems. In
addition to this, we are currently applying these techniques for different type problems.
•
Moumita Mandal: Broad area of research is Numerical Functional Analysis. In particular, spectral projection methods
for solving integral equations and integro-Differential equations, fractional integro-differential equations.
•

•
Nil Kamal Hazra: My research areas are Robust Statistical Inference, Sequential Analysis, Applied Probability, Statistical
Learning
•
Pradip Sasmal: My research areas are Finite Frame Theory, Compressed Sensing, Physics Informed Neural Networks
(PINNs), Reinforcement Learning (RL) and Light-Weight Neural Networks.
•
Puneet Sharma: I broadly work in the area of Topological Dynamics. I am currently investigating dynamics of triangular
maps and dynamical nature of algebraic structures associated with general dynamical systems.
•
Subhash Bhagat: My primary research interests lie in the areas of distributed systems and algorithms. In particular, I am
interested in the following areas: Distributed algorithms for Swarm Robots and Autonomous Multi-Agent systems.
Internet of Robotic Things (IoRT) and Autonomous Mobile Robotic Sensors. Distributed Network algorithms. Security in
Distributed Computing
•
Sukhendu Ghosh: My ongoing research includes Hydrodynamic Stability Analysis, Mathematical Modelling and
Computations, Lie Groups Analysis of Differential Equations. My research group focuses on the mathematical modelling
and analysis of various fluid flow problems as well as other complicated physical problems.
•
Tuhina Mukherjee: My research focuses on analysis of PDEs as a broad area of research where in particular, we study
existence, non-existence and regularity of weak solutions to given PDEs alongwith their characteristics.
•
V. V. M. S. Chandramouli: The central theme of the one-dimensional dynamical theory is the geometric rigidity of the
attractors. The main technique is renormalization. Renormalization is a method to study asymptotic small scale geometry
of the attractor of one-dimensional systems which are at the transition from simple to chaotic dynamics. The existence of
a unique renormalization fixed point which is also hyperbolic among generic smooth enough maps plays a crucial role in
the renormalization theory. It gives the universality phenomenon and rigidity of the attractor. My contributions show the
breakdown of uniqueness and rigidity, when one approaches from below the minimal smoothness thresholds. And finally
we show that the renormalization operator acting on a low smoothness space of maps has infinite topological entropy.
Which describes the non-rigidity of renormalization in contrast to the Rigidity phenomenon in one-dimensional
dynamics.
•
Vivek Vijay: My research interests lie in the broad area of Categorical Data Analysis, with some applications in
collapsibility of contingency tables, and forecasting of financial data, solar data and health care data using Machine
Learning and Statistical Techniques.
•
Kiran Meena: My research interests lie in Differential, Riemannian, Complex, and Contact Geometries. Precisely, I am
working on the geometric aspects of some smooth manifolds and space forms by using various smooth mappings.
New Laboratory Facilities:
•
The Department of Mathematics has established a dedicated computational lab to support the computational needs of
M.Tech. Data Science, M.Sc., and Ph.D. Mathematics students. Recently, the lab has been upgraded with the addition of
10 high-performance desktops, along with a powerful server and a GPU-equipped workstation to enhance capabilities for
data-intensive research and advanced simulations.

Associate Dean, Computer Centre (ADCC)
•
Nurture an exciting and flexible academic ecosystem inculcating design thinking with a strong 
fundamental background in Mechanical engineering
•
Pursue indigenous research to cultivate technological solutions addressing current demand in the allied 
areas of national and global interest
•
Establish state of the art labs, thematic research and workshop facilities to address the needs of application 
oriented as well as blue-sky research engagements of the department
•
Establish research collaborations with industries and academia to provide solution to socio-technical problems.
•
Achieve maximum possible financial independence through department-level resource generation.
DEPARTMENT OF MECHANICAL ENGINEERING
The Department of Mechanical Engineering at IIT Jodhpur strives to create a unique and flexible academic and 
research ecosystem that nurtures sustainable human resource development and drives technological progress in 
critical areas such as Advanced Manufacturing, Automation, Energy and Water, Micro-Nano Engineering, Smart 
Structures, Robotics, and Mobility. With a curriculum that blends Design Thinking with a solid grounding in 
Mechanical Engineering principles, the department empowers students to pursue innovative academic and 
professional paths. This holistic approach enables students to not only excel in traditional Mechanical 
Engineering but also delve into cutting-edge interdisciplinary fields such as Artificial Intelligence (AI), Internet of 
Things (IoT), Cyber- Physical Systems (CPS), Augmented Reality/Virtual Reality (AR/VR), Data Science, and 
Robotics. These advancements open up a wide range of career prospects for graduates. The department's mission 
and 
vision 
further 
underscore 
this 
commitment. 
Vision: Excellence in focus areas of advance manufacturing, mobility, energy and water, micro-nano 
engineering and smart structures and mechanics through continuous pedagogical research endeavours. 
The department is guided by the following mission statements:

Faculty Awards and Achievements during 2024-2025
•
Prof. Rahul Chhibber has been awarded W. H. Hobart Memorial Award from American Welding Society
▪
Prof. Rahul Chhibber, Professor, Mechanical Engineering Department, has been awarded the W. H. 
Hobart Memorial Award from American Welding Society. This award is presented in memory of William 
H. Hobart, Sr., and is sponsored by Hobart Brothers Company. It is awarded to the authors of the 
paper published in the Welding Journal during the previous calendar year that describes the best 
contribution to pipe welding.
•
Dr. Shrutidhara Sarma Selected for INAE Young Associateship 2024
▪
Dr. Shrutidhara Sarma, Assistant Professor, Department of Mechanical Engineering, Indian 
Institute of Technology Jodhpur and PI of FERN Lab (https://www.shrutidhara.com/) has been 
honoured with the prestigious INAE Young Associateship 2024 (https://www.inae.in/young-
criteria/) in recognition to her outstanding contributions in Mechanical Engineering.
▪
The recognition will be presented at the INAE Annual Convention 2024 and the recipients will be 
formally inducted as INAE Young Associates. The Indian National Academy of Engineering (INAE), 
established in 1987, consists of the country’s most accomplished engineers, scientists, and 
technologists, spanning all areas of engineering. INAE functions as an apex body and promotes the 
advancement of engineering, technology, and related sciences, with a focus on addressing key challenges 
of national significance.
•

Anup Maurya, a Ph.D graduate of Mechanical Engineering Department worked under the supervision of 
Prof. Rahul Chhibber and Dr. Chandan Pandey, has been awarded C. V. Raman Gold Medal from IIT 
Jodhpur

23rd ISME International Conference on Recent Advances in Mechanical Engineering
o
23rd ISME International Conference – 2025 will be held in the picturesque pink city of India, Jaipur 
from December 17 - 19, 2025. The intention is to setup an environment for knowledge sharing 
between international and national academia and industry experts. To blend some outdoor fun with 
the inspiring keynote addresses and expert lectures, a half day city tour has been planned on Saturday, 
December 19. The conference organizers look forward to all those working in various domains of 
Mechanical Engineering to showcase their excellence as well as challenges faced in diverse 
technological advancements. The conference will cover a wide array of topics listed on page 4 of this 
brochure. The special theme of this conference is integration of AI/ML into mechanical engineering. 
This conference which is 23 in series of ISME conferences is being jointly organized by IIT Jodhpur, 
LNMIIT Jaipur and MNIT Jaipur under the aegis of Indian Society of Mechanical Engineers. (Website: 
https://lnmiit.ac.in/isme-2025/)

Department of Metallurgical & Material Engineering

DEPARTMENT OF METALLURGICAL AND 
MATERIALS ENGINEERING
The Department of Materials Engineering at IIT Jodhpur was established in 2017 with a vision of imparting high-
quality education in the areas of Materials Engineering to address continuously evolving demands of new 
materials in the fast-evolving sectors such as, energy, aerospace, defence, healthcare, transport, etc. The 
department is committed to high-quality education and research in the broad area of Materials Engineering. The 
department continuously strives for excellence in teaching and research through innovative pedagogy and 
curriculum, by undertaking interdisciplinary projects, and through active collaborations with industries, R&D 
labs, and academia. By enabling the students to think independently and equipping them with relevant skill 
sets, our goal is to encourage the graduates to innovate and address present-day materials challenges to meet 
the needs of the country. The department is currently offering degree programs namely, B.Tech., M.Tech., Ph.D. 
and M.Tech.-Ph.D. in Materials Engineering which are designed through a unique combination of 
foundational courses, core courses and electives from the following four thematic areas or streams: 
Structural Materials Materials Processing, Additive Manufacturing, Phase Transformations, Deformation 
Behavior and Microstructure evolution, Failure of Materials, High Temperature Materials, Materials Degradation.

techniques, Principles of Process Metallurgy, Kinetics of Metallurgical Processes.

Faculty Awards and Achievements during 2024-2025
Student's Awards and Achievements during 2024-2025
Research Highlights:
The Department of Metallurgical and Materials Engineering has made significant strides in research and innovation during 
the academic year 2024–25. The department published over 90 peer-reviewed journal articles in reputed international 
journals such as Scripta Materialia, Journal of Alloys and Compounds, Surface & Coatings Technology, Advanced Energy 
Materials, ACS Applied Nano Materials, Journal of Magnesium and Alloys, and Materials Today Communications. The 
core research areas spanned across High Entropy Alloys, Additive Manufacturing, Battery Materials, Biomaterials, 
Quantum Materials, 2D Materials, and Thermoelectric Materials, with interdisciplinary efforts integrating computational 
modeling techniques such as DFT, Molecular Dynamics, and CALPHAD, alongside advanced characterization tools like 
TEM, APT, and XRD.
The department currently handles more than 25 sponsored research projects, with cumulative funding of approximately 
7.5 crore, supported by premier agencies including SERB, DST, BRNS, DBT, MSME, ARDB, and ISRO-RAC. Noteworthy
projects include the design of superalloys for 3D printed turbine components (ARDB), porosity prediction in additive
manufacturing using in-situ diagnostics and CALPHAD (ISRO-RAC), oxidation and quenching behavior of Zr alloys
(BRNS), and innovative projects on green ammonia electrocatalysts, 2D borophene synthesis, and damage-tolerant HEAs.
On the collaborative front, the department maintains active international research partnerships with the University at
Buffalo (USA), Chalmers University of Technology (Sweden), and National Chung Hsing University (Taiwan). National
research engagements include premier R&D institutions like IISc Bangalore, IIT Kanpur, IIT Bombay, DMRL, IGCAR,
VSSC, and CSIR-NML, as well as industry partners such as Eaton India, Tata Steel, Amace Solutions, Intech Additive
Solutions, and Bharat Forge.

In terms of student research excellence, the department boasts over 15 awards won by students at prominent 
conferences including ICAMC, NSRS, NMD-ATM, and FFIA, with three students awarded the prestigious 
PMRF fellowship. International exposure for students was facilitated through exchange programs at the 
University at Buffalo and the University of North Texas (USA), as well as a SERB-sponsored international travel 
grant.
The department also played a proactive role in community engagement and knowledge dissemination by organizing 
a range of workshops and symposia, such as the IIAP-HEA 2024 Symposium on High Entropy Alloys, the 
MatRS-2024 Materials Research Symposium, and technical workshops on X-ray Diffraction, Spectroscopy, 
and Additive Manufacturing. Additionally, a SPARC-sponsored international workshop on HEAs was held in 
collaboration with MNIT Jaipur, and Industry Day 2023 paved the way for the upcoming Industry Academia 
Interaction planned for 2025.
New Laboratory Facilities:
During the financial year 2024–25, the Department of Metallurgical and Materials Engineering at IIT Jodhpur 
undertook significant expansion and development of its laboratory infrastructure to support cutting-edge 
research and advanced training. A major highlight was the establishment and enhancement of the Structural 
Materials Research Laboratory, with a lab-scale hot rolling mill currently under procurement. This facility focuses 
on alloy development for aerospace, automotive, and biomedical applications, particularly in the domains of high 
entropy and lightweight alloys.
Simultaneously, 
the 
Functional 
Materials 
Research Laboratory was significantly upgraded 
to 
support 
the 
integrated 
synthesis, 
characterization, 
and 
device fabrication of 2D 
and quantum materials. Key additions include a 
64-core high-performance computational server 
for 
DFT 
and 
thermoelectric 
calculations, 
equipment 
for 
gas 
sensing 
and 
battery 
testing, 
a photolithography 
setup, 
a 
Hall 
measurement system, and an M–H hysteresis 
loop tracer. The lab also developed expertise 
in HRTEM image simulation and processing, 
enabling atomic-scale analysis of materials. The 
Computational Materials Engineering Laboratory 
was 
further 
enhanced 
with 
additional high-performance workstations and 
updated licenses for key software packages such 
as 
Quantum 
Espresso, 
VASP, 
LAMMPS, 
COMSOL 
Multiphysics, 
and Thermo-Calc, 
supporting 
research 
in 
alloy 
design, phase 
stability, and process simulations.
The Heat Treatment Laboratory also saw notable upgrades, including the installation of a high-temperature 
furnace (up to 1800°C), a two-chamber salt bath furnace, and a vacuum sealing setup, facilitating advanced 
thermal processing of steels, aluminium, titanium, and high entropy alloys.

administrators.

Department of Physic

DEPARTMENT OF PHYSICS
The Department of Physics at IIT Jodhpur is dedicated to excellence in both fundamental and applied 
physics, with research strengths in Condensed Matter and Plasma Physics, High Energy Physics and 
Astrophysics, Quantum Physics, and Optics and Photonics. The department offers Undergraduate, Master, and 
Doctoral programs in Physics, with a focus on experiential learning through laboratory experiments, hands-on 
activities, and student-led seminars. Additionally, the Department offers core and elective science courses for 
undergraduate Engineering students, fostering interdisciplinary knowledge. With a strong emphasis on 
fundamental research and innovation, the department equips graduates for leadership roles in cutting-edge 
research and technology development. Driven by a vision of academic and research excellence, the 
department strives to contribute to emerging technologies and scientific advancements. Through a flexible and 
modern curriculum, the Department is committed to shaping the future of physics at the intersection of science 
and engineering.
Vision of the Department: 
To achieve excellence in teaching and research in fundamental as well as applied physics with focus on High 
Energy & Astrophysics, Quantum Information Processing, Energy, Functional Materials & Devices
Department Research Activities: The Condensed Matter and Plasma Physics Group at IIT Jodhpur 
focuses 
on 
experimental 
and 
computational 
research 
in 
energy 
materials, 
photovoltaics, 
nanostructures, 
and 
cold 
plasma technologies, addressing fundamental scientific and technological 
challenges in energy, climate change, and sustainable growth. With interdisciplinary labs and national and 
international collaborations, the group is at the forefront of cutting-edge research. The High Energy 
Physics and Astrophysics Group explores astrophysics and particle physics to understand fundamental 
interactions and the evolution of the universe, participating in global collaborations such as the Belle II project 
in Japan, and GRAPES-3. The Quantum Physics Group explores nonclassical evolution, PT-symmetric 
quantum physics, quantum thermodynamics, and quantum optics, aiming to advance quantum technology 
through state engineering. Meanwhile, the Optics and Photonics Group focuses on terahertz technology, 
ultrafast optical techniques, spectroscopy, specialty optical fibers, and quantum confinement, contributing 
to both fundamental discoveries and technological advancements in optics.FACULTY MEMBERS:

Additional information:
Ashutosh Memorial Gold Medal: 
Prof. Ashutosh Kumar Alok, being one of the most passionate theoretical physicists one could come 
across, had a distinctive aura that spread reverence around his colleagues and students. We were not only 
in awe of his power of thinking and formulating foundational leaps in particle physics, but also beyond his 
brilliant mind, he was much more. To honor his legacy and to inspire future generations to follow in his footsteps, 
we concluded to set up an Ashutosh Memorial Gold Medal—an annual award recognizing excellence in the MSc 
(Physics) program. Prof. Ashutosh played a pivotal role in shaping the MSc (Physics) curriculum since its 
inception in 2015 and was instrumental in launching the BS (Physics) program in 2022 during his tenure as 
Head of the Department. His global research collaborations and profound impact on foundational aspects of 
particle physics stand as a testament to his brilliant mind and unwavering commitment to the advancement of 
science.

Research Highlights:
Mr. Shubham Chamola (PhD student of Dr. Shahab Ahmad): Published in Advanced Functional Materials 
(Impact 
Factor: 
18, 
https://advanced.onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/full/10.1002/adfm.202414913) 
on 
the 
development of Sb2S3 nanorods for photoenhanced Li-ion batteries. His work demonstrates a single-material 
photobattery capable of simultaneous solar energy harvesting and storage, advancing off-grid energy solutions. 
The research offers a cost-effective, sustainable solution for powering low-power, off-grid IoT applications.
Mr. Rashid Malik Ansari (PhD student of Dr. Shahab Ahmad): Published in Small (Impact Factor: 13, 
https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/10.1002/smll.202401350 
) 
on 
developing Ruddlesden–Popper 2D 
Perovskite-MoS2 Hybrid Heterojunction Photocathodes for Efficient and Scalable Photo-Rechargeable Li-Ion 
Batteries. His work offers a novel approach to develop type-II perovskite heterostructures for the 
development of efficient Photobatteries.

Research and Teaching Innovations) Biennial conference from 10-13 December, 2024. The conference was sponsored by
GALE and had plenary sessions by renowned DH scholars from both, India and abroad.
We invited nine plenary speakers for the conference. Prof. Nirmala Menon, IIT Indore, Dr. Vinayak Dasgupta, Shiv
Nadar University, Dr. Shanmugapriya, IIT Dhanbad, Dr. Mayurakshi Chaudhuri, Flame University, Dr. Maya Dodd,
Flame University, and Dr. Souvik Mukherjee, Centre for Studies in Social Sciences delivered plenary talks during the
conference. We also had three international plenary speakers: Prof. Leonardo Flores, Appalachian State University, Dr.
Dibyadyuti Roy, Leeds University and Dr. Setsuko Yokoyama, Singapore University of Technology.
•
The conference witnessed many fascinating papers presented by young research scholars as well as established voices
within the field of Digital Humanities in India and abroad. GALE group conducted a workshop during the conference
in which Mr. Mark Richardson spoke on ‘Introduction to Gale, digitisation and Gale as infrastructure.’ Mr. Chris
Houghton spoke on the topic ‘Building Sustainable Ecosystems: Using Gale to support Indian Digital Humanities
Infrastructure,’ and Ms. Mickey Mehta provided a demo on Gale databases. During the conference, significant
workshops were also organised such as a workshop on QGIS software and a workshop by MaTra Lab for analysing
multilingual audiovisual data.
•
This is one of the first international conferences hosted by Digital Humanities, IDRP division, and it provided a lot of
visibility to the Digital Humanities programme at IIT Jodhpur.

Center for AIOT and Applications
The Internet of Things (IoT) has captured significant interest across various sectors, including smart 
agriculture, transportation, environmental monitoring, smart cities, smart grid, autonomous vehicles, 
healthcare, and industrial applications. Central to IoT functionality are sensors that need to be both highly 
sensitive and selective to effectively interact with their environment. Furthermore, the data these sensors collect 
is essential for enhancing the intelligence of processes and systems. IoT encompasses a broad range of disciplines, 
from material science to data analytics, all vital for developing IoT systems. To address these complex needs, 
an Inter-Disciplinary Research Platform (IDRP) has been established for the Center for AIOT and 
Applications. This platform aims to integrate technologies comprehensively, fostering research and 
development across sectors like Industry 4.0, health, and infrastructure, which includes safety and environmental 
monitoring. The collaborative R&D ecosystem in Jodhpur, which brings together institutions like IITJ, AIIMS, 
NLU, and Police University, is poised to drive innovation in AIOT in areas such as healthcare, environment, and 
cybersecurity.
Figure 1: Internet of Things (IoT) and its applications
The infographic( Shown in Figure 1) depicts various aspects of the Internet of Things (IoT) and its 
applications across multiple domains. On the left side, key technological components are listed, such as Sensors, 
Communication, Computing, AI/ML, AR/VR, Security, and Energy Harvesting. The center of the image displays 
specific application areas, categorized into Manufacturing, Energy, Mobility, Healthcare, Infrastructure, 
Logistics, Living, and Agriculture, with examples like Industry 4.0, Smart Grid, Intelligent Mobility, and 
Precision Agriculture. On the right, the outcomes or benefits of IoT integration are shown, including 
Intelligence, Efficiency, Connectivity, Transparency, and Flexibility. This layout illustrates how foundational 
technologies enable diverse applications, which in turn generate various beneficial outcomes.

Figure 2: Design aspects of IoT

The design aspects ( Shown in Figure 2) of IoT focus on embedded AI and efficient data management within constrained 
resources, highlighting the importance of secure, scalable architectures and edge computing for real-time processing. The 
key applications of IoT encompass practical deployments like Industry 4.0, which integrates digital twins and predictive 
maintenance, and Smart City technologies for optimizing urban infrastructure. Smart Interfaces involve enhancing user 
interaction through AR/VR, haptic feedback, sensor fusion, and robotic e-skin, making IoT devices more intuitive and 
effective in real-world applications. Together, these elements define the multifaceted scope of IoT technology.

Quantum Information & Computation (QIC)
Over the last century, Quantum Mechanics has emerged as a fundamental ingredient for understanding various 
facets of nature such as atomic and sub-atomic physics, quantum optics, and a plethora of phenomena in condensed 
matter physics. Modern developments in computing could be said to have started from the work of Alan Turing, 
while information theory was put on the pedestal of modern science by the efforts of Claude Shannon. The 
amalgamation of quantum physics with computing and information theory could be historically traced from the 
works of EPR (Einstein, Podolsky, and Rosen), followed by that of John Bell and culminating in efforts made by 
Charles Bennett. This was further cemented by the efforts of William Wootters. In the last three decades, the world 
has witnessed enormous progress on the theoretical front to investigate the foundations of quantum information, 
and to analyze the potentials offered by entanglement and nonlocal correlations towards computing. The ongoing 
debates, studies, and creative intellect paved the way for a new computing paradigm with a promise of speed-up, 
efficiency, and enhanced security. In fact, the experimental developments over the last few decades have brought 
the subject of quantum information and computation to the threshold of technology development.
Handling, manipulating, and processing quantum information require control and protection of nonlocal correlations 
over quantum channels. The fragile nature of these correlations coupled with uncontrollable interactions with 
surroundings make the problem of scalability exponentially challenging. The increase in technological difficulties with 
the increase in the number of qubits should not be surprising considering that complexity is the characteristic trait of 
the theory in place. In fact, it is the complexity and potential therein that motivate academicians, industries, and 
entrepreneurs to invest in the intellect and generate funding to resolve theoretical and technological challenges. 
Apart from academia across the globe, tech giants such as IBM, Google, Microsoft, D-Wave, Intel, Regetti, 
QuintessenceLabs, Hewlett Packard, Ion Q, Cambridge quantum computing Quantum Biosystems, and many more 
are addressing the issues related to control, gate fidelity and scalability- quantum error correction. Moreover, the 
Government of India has taken cognizance of the area and initiated a new research program on Quantum Enabled 
Science & Technology (QuEST), and in a similar way, the Ministry of Electronics and Information Technology 
(MeitY) has taken various initiatives.

Description of Research Groups
The Quantum Information and Computation (QIC) group at IIT Jodhpur is working towards analyzing classical 
and quantum correlations from the perspective of a practical interface between quantum optics and quantum 
information processing. Such correlations occupy a central position in the quest for understanding and 
harvesting the power of quantum mechanics and the fundamentals of quantum information processing. As a group, 
we are addressing some of the key issues in characterizing multiqubit entanglement. From the application's 
perspective, the spectrum includes but is not limited to quantum key distribution, quantum dense coding, 
quantum teleportation, quantum cryptography, quantum game theory and quantum secure communication, 
quantum sensing, and materials research for quantum technologies. For a practical implementation of any quantum 
information task, it is important to consider the role of noise in the chosen task. The group is interested in the 
systematic study of quantum information and computation in realistic scenarios, including the effect of ambient 
noise, using ideas and techniques of Open Quantum Systems.

Interface of Particle Physics with Quantum Information, Theories developed for:
A. Neutrino oscillations imply quantum correlations and vice versa.
B.

4.
Quantum Thermodynamics:
A. Impact of non-Markovian effects on a quantum heat engine probed.
B.
The dynamics of a simplified version of a quantum thermal diode studied.
5.
Quantum Optics:
A. Properties of engineered quantum states studied.
B.
Dynamics of Tavis-Cummings model in the context of cavity quantum electrodynamics probed.
6.
Entanglement and Nonlocality in Multiqubit systems:
A. An efficient generic approach based on cluster coefficients to classify and quantify entanglement and nonlocal
correlations in multiqubit states is developed

2. Academic Programs
2.1 Ph.D. Program
The Ph.D. program offered by the IDRP on RMS is one of the few nationwide programs where students can earn a doctorate 
in Robotics/Mobility Systems. The program is inherently interdisciplinary, bringing together areas of research that would 
otherwise be spread across different departments or separate universities.
2.2 M.Tech. Program
To meet the increasing demand for engineers with diverse backgrounds in the field of robotic and mobility systems, and to 
support relevant research and development, an M.Tech. Programme in Robotics and Mobility System is designed. The 
program offers micro specializations in:
•
Autonomous Mobile Robots (AMRs)
•
Unmanned Aerial Vehicles (UAVs)
•
Electric Vehicles (EVs)
2.3 B.Tech. Specialization
An interdisciplinary specialization in robotics is offered for B.Tech. students to provide an understanding of the field to 
those interested in pursuing careers or post-graduate degrees in robotics.
3. Research and Projects
3.1 M.Tech. Student Projects
3.1.1 Performance Evaluation of Quadcopter Rotor With Blockage in Inflow
Student: Rajesh Kumar Samantaray (M22RM006)
Supervisor: C. Venkatesan
This project involves making an experimental setup to study the impact of the proximity of the rotor to the ground on 
thrust, torque, and power. Results indicate increased thrust with decreased ground distance, while torque has an 
increasing-decreasing trend. Further experiments simulate blockage and impact on rotor thrust and torque.
3.1.2 Human in Loop Control of Mobile Manipulator System Using MPC
Student: Ashutosh Sahu (M22RM001)
Supervisors: Dr. Suril Vijaykumar Shah & Dr. Niladri Sekhar Tripathy
The project explores Model Predictive Control (MPC) for mobile manipulators, employed separately on the kinematic 
model of a mobile robot (Turtlebot3) and manipulator (Kinova Gen3 Lite). A framework integrates human-in-the-loop 
control via an Xbox One Controller for object-picking tasks, showcasing its implementation on actual hardware.
3.1.3 Monocular Depth Estimation
Student: Rahul Harish Madaan (M22RM008)
Supervisor: Dr. Malyala Pavana Ravi Sai Kiran
Robotics & Mobility Systems (RMS)
1. Introduction
The Inter-Disciplinary Research Platform (IDRP) on Robotics and Mobility Systems (RMS) is a multidisciplinary initiative 
focused on solving open research problems requiring an integrated approach through the fusion of knowledge from 
multiple fields.
1.1 Vision
Advance the interdisciplinary fields of robotics and mobility systems through development in modelling, control, 
multimodal perception, communication, AI/ML, and energy management systems to solve technological challenges in 
civil and military sectors and develop state-of-the-art applications.
1.2 Missions

This project implemented a zoe depth model and a two-view structure from motion technique for indoor drone 
navigation. These approaches enhance the drone’s spatial awareness and maneuverability indoors, providing a 
comprehensive solution for accurate indoor navigation.
3.1.4 Real Time 3D Scene Reconstruction and Localization of Autonomous Ground Vehicle
Student: Karan Bhakuni (M22RM003)
Supervisor: Dr. Rajendra Nagar
The project involves implementing SLAM using 3D LiDAR technology to map unknown environments 
and simultaneously localize a mobile robot. Algorithms include classical ICP for raw point cloud registration and 
Neural Distance Fields to enhance visual clarity. A research paper was submitted to ECCV 2024 conference on 
employing NDF on raw point clouds.
3.1.5 Object Tracking and Image Deblurring for Vision Based Path Planning
Student: Soham Padhye (M22RM007)
Supervisor: Dr. Himanshu Kumar
This project developed an image enhancement system for a fast-moving robot addressing motion blur. It improved 
image quality to enhance the detection of robust keypoints and developed a novel image processing algorithm to 
predict motion blur kernels for sharp image recovery using an Interaction matrix.
3.1.6 Autonomous Image-basedWeed Detection System for Smart Agriculture
Student: Mahendra G L (M22RM004)
Supervisor: Arpit Khandelwal
This project involves an autonomous image-based weed detection system for smart agriculture using YOLO 
models trained on a local farm dataset. The system classifies weeds from crop plants using images captured by Pi 
cameras or mobile devices, enabling accurate real-time weed detection.
3.1.7 Deep Learning Based Robotics Application
Student: K Vamsi (M22RM002)
Supervisor: Binod Kumar
This project aimed to develop a robot platform capable of identifying and extinguishing fires at an early stage. 
SLAM algorithms were employed for mapping and localization tasks, while Heat Maps and YOLO were used for fire 
detection. The system enables autonomous navigation to predefined locations for firefighting.
3.2 Ph.D. Research
3.2.1 Learning Vision-Based Robotic Manipulation Tasks Sequentially in Offline Reinforcement Learning Settings 
Student: Sudhir Pratap Yadav
Supervisors: Dr. Suril V. Shah and Dr. Rajendra Nagar
Paper: Yadav SP, Nagar R, Shah SV. Learning vision-based robotic manipulation tasks sequentially in offline 
reinforcement learning settings. Robotica. Published online 2024:1-16.
This research investigates the effectiveness of regularisation-based methods like synaptic intelligence for 
sequentially learning image-based robotic manipulation tasks in an offline-RL setup. The study evaluates the 
performance against challenges of sequential learning, including catastrophic forgetting and forward knowledge 
transfer.

Smart Healthcare
The Interdisciplinary Research Platform (IDRP) in Smart Healthcare at IIT Jodhpur is focused on advancing 
healthcare through a multidisciplinary approach. It brings together experts from various fields like basic 
science and engineering such as biology, chemistry, computer Science, electronics and electrical 
engineering, mechanical engineering and material science to develop innovative solutions for modern 
healthcare challenges.
Key objectives and focus areas of IDRP Smart Healthcare include:

•
Develop scientific and technological tools including certain specialized payloads for the furtherance of research 
in basic or fundamental science, particularly in the exploration of the Universe.
•
Technology advancement can be achieved with

Pure technological development

Translation of basic research into technology.
The program will be based on system approach involving multidisciplinary subjects wherein a set of complex 
problems pertaining to the Space Science and Technology will be taken up involving several sub-activities 
such as design and development of sub-components including materials modelling, experimental realization, 
component modelling and fabrication, integration, and its validation as a complete system/sub-system.

Space Science & Technology
The space science and technology (SST) inter disciplinary research platform (IDRP) at IIT Jodhpur has been formed 
in 2019 to cater the growing demands on space sector research in the country. The proposed research programme 
on Space Science and Technology will be a collective multi-disciplinary effort to address key scientific and 
engineering issues in understanding and exploiting space. The space being so vast and varied with almost infinite 
number of stellar objects and perhaps a greater number of unknowns than knowns, offers huge opportunities to 
carry out fundamental research to develop better understanding of the Universe. Further, space also offers wide 
range of opportunities for its exploitation for a number of technological applications such as space vehicles, 
satellite technologies, remote sensing using sensors operating over a range of wavelength regions including 
visible, infrared, microwave, etc. It comprises of both the science as well as engineering/technology components.

Shock Waves and High-Speed Flow (SWAHS) Lab
The SWAHS lab tries to advance the frontiers of research activities and technology development in the field of 
Aerospace and Defence sector. We also focus on extending the high-speed flows and shock waves research to other 
applications such as Refrigeration systems, Bio-Medical engineering, Industrial processing, Water processing 
etc. Some of the existing research activities undertaken in these directions are, Supersonic Intakes, 
Supersonic Air-Fuel Mixing in Scramjet Combustors, Flow control and Actuators, Gas Turbine Cooling, 
Electric Propulsion Systems, Shock & Blast Wave Attenuation, Shock waves applications in Bio-Medical 
Engineering, Solar Ejector Refrigeration, Steam Ejector based Water Purification etc.

School of Artificial Intelligence and Data Science

SCHOOL OF ARTIFICIAL INTELLIGENCE AND DATA SCIENCE
Breakthroughs in AI and Data Science are key to shaping the future technological landscape. AI and Data Science 
is impacting progress of diverse disciplines of natural sciences, different fields of engineering and medicine, social 
sciences, and economics. In order to be at the forefront of this emerging technological frontier, School of Artificial 
Intelligence and Data Science (AIDE) was established at IIT Jodhpur in July 2020 with the vision to advance the 
field of AI and Data Sciences for the good of humanity. The School aims to play a leading role in research, 
teaching and training in AI and its applications. The School also focuses on developing AI based technologies 
aligned to the locally and nationally relevant problems and challenges. AIDE School brings together faculty from 
diverse disciplines with shared interests in fundamental challenges in AI and Data Science to make significant 
contributions in this field. Currently there are 31 faculty in the School which includes 19 affiliated faculty from 10 
different departments and schools of IIT Jodhpur and 4 adjunct faculty from different national and international 
institutes.

Conferences and invited talks organized at IITJ
Thar Talk Series: AI and Beyond, in collaboration with Jodhpur City Knowledge and Innovation Foundation
The Thar Talk Series aims to organize webinars on the role of Artificial Intelligence and Data Science in solving the current 
problems and shaping the future technological landscape of various fields of science, engineering, and public health. The 
series focuses on multidisciplinary emerging themes and fundamental issues, and explores pathbreaking possibilities in 
various disciplines of Engineering and Sciences. Under the Thar Talk series, we invite distinguished speakers from around 
the world working in the areas of but not limited to: Brain Science, Intelligent Infrastructure, Mathematical and 
Computational Economics, Smart Business Analytics, Autonomous Robot Systems, Computer Vision, AI Hardware, 
Chemical Process Modeling, Computational Material Science, AI for Social Good, AI and Emotion, etc. In the past year, we 
organized twelve talks which were open to the national and international audiences. The details of past talks are available 
on AIDE School website (https://aide.iitj.ac.in/index.php/talk). Full recordings of the talks are available publicly on 
YouTube. (Link: https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLHASPzwmCK-ELDjbqJu91_uf2K4zUKl6R).
