Laboratories and Equipment
Center on Brain Science & Applications
Cognitive Engineering Lab facility at IIT Jodhpur - This lab is equipped with 128 channel high density EEG recording 
system, Wireless EEG headset, Tobii pro fusion Eye-tracker system with high sampling frequency, Virtual Reality system, 
Neurostimulation devices including Transcranial Magnetic Stimulation (TMS) system along with Xensor; 
neuronavigation, and digitimer, neurostym tES system with various low intensity electrical stimulation protocols tDCS, 
tACS & tRNS, 32 channel TMS compatible EEG system with enhanced artifact suppression, Brainvision Cap Trak 
System, and a variety of stimulus presentation software for stimulus design for behavioral recordings and assessment. The 
facility is currently being used to study naturalistic image and audio-visual stimulus processing, Visual and Auditory 
perception and steady state processing, working and episodic memory processing and developmental changes associated 
with speech, language, perceptual processing in children, adolescents, adults of different age groups to record and analyze 
brain signals and study systematically behavior coupling and developmental alterations in cognitive processes.
EEG Recording Device (Brain Vision actiCHamp Plus): The device provides a seamless 128 channel EEG recording with 
a maximum sampling frequency of 25 KHz. The device comes with a powerful lithium-ion battery pack. It works with a 
software interface called Brain Vision Recorder and Analyzer to support data recording and analysis. 
(https://www.brainproducts.com/solutions/actichamp/)

Eye Tracker (Tobii Pro Fusion Screen-based): The device detects and 
tracks the eye movements using the pupil center corneal reflection 
(PCCR) technique. It supports multiple sampling rates up to 250 Hz

Tobii Pro Lab to support experiment design and data analysis.

Transcranial Magnetic Stimulation (TMS) System (By Magstim): The 
Magstim Bistim2 is used for the stimulation of peripheral nerves and the 
human cortex for diagnostic purposes. The Magstim Bistim2 consists of 
two units along with a connecting module that enables the output from 
two Magstim units to output into a single stimulating coil as a single 
high-energy pulse or a pair of individual spaced pulses. The TMS device 
is capable of stimulating by inducing small currents in the nerve using a 
brief pulse of electromagnetic energy. The device is useful for 
Intracortical 
facilitation 
and 
inhibition 
research 
(https://www.magstim.com/row-en/)
Virtual Reality System (Meta Quest Pro VR Headset): The Meta Quest 
Pro is a mixed reality (MR) headset developed by Reality Labs, a division 
of Meta Platforms. The headset contains internal sensors that are used 
for eye and face tracking, primarily for use with avatars. The Quest Pro 
has a thinner lens enclosure and a more visor-like form factor that does 
not obscure the entirety of the user’s peripheral vision in contrast to the 
other VR headsets. The lenses can be adjusted for interpupillary distance 
and can be moved forward and backward. The Quest Pro uses Touch Pro 
controllers, having a more compact design with upgraded haptics with 
onboard motion tracking using embedded cameras and processors. The 
controllers are also rechargeable via the headset’s charging dock.
(https://www.meta.com/quest/quest-pro/; 
https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meta_Quest_Pro)

BrainVision CapTrak System (Brain Products): It is a quick and 
precise electrode localization system for active electrodes. It takes 5 
minutes to scan 128 electrode positions. The system has a light, hand-
held scanner with two integrated cameras and intuitive software. 
The scanned electrode location file in the format (.bvct) can be 
exported to software like BrainStorm and/or EEGlab for source 
localization 
studies. 
(https://www.brainproducts.com/solutions/
captrak/)
Bittium NeurOne Tesla TMS Compatible EEG System: The outcomes 
of the stimulation can be measured using TMS-compatible EEG 
systems, which are specially designed to synchronize with TMS and 
suppress artifacts caused by the stimulation. By using this system 
alongside TMS, we can observe how the brain responds to 
stimulation across cortical networks. Additionally, EMG data can be 
acquired using a Digitimer system, to precisely measure muscle 
responses during this phase.
Center on AI & Precision Medicine
Introduction:
There is a continuous rise in the prevalence of common and complex diseases with a substantial reduction in health 
longevity which poses a considerable economic burden. In the precision medicine era, there has been a paradigm shift in 
healthcare wherein we are moving from a reactive to more proactive management with a precision component in all 
aspects of P5 (Predictive, Preventive, Personalized, Participatory, Promotive) medicine. Traditional medicine systems 
such as Ayurveda provide a system’s understanding of an individual wherein individual-specific health baselines inform 
about response and trajectory in geo-spatio-temporal dimensions for pre-emptive management of lifestyle and nutrition. 
Disease trajectories assessment and treatment are individual centric manner and dealt with as moving targets. There are 
also unique therapeutic modalities such as Panchakarma, multicomponent single, and poly herbo-metallic formulations 
along with different preparations and modes of administration for diverse therapies. Thus, multiple options are now 
available from modern and traditional AYUSH systems for the management of diseases. However, due to limited cross-
talk, most often a patient who has the least expertise self-evolves an integrative approach to the management of health.
AyurTech: Setting up
•
Computer-based phenomics, IoT-based digital devices & AI-powered
Prakriti assessment and Vikriti diagnosis
•
Interoperable platform for unifying ontologies
•
Devices & systems for Ayurveda drug standardization and quality
control
•
Drug-disease networks compendium for drug signatures & Ayurveda
based formulations for poly-pharmacology & repurposing
•
Capacity Building
A formalized framework that allows one to assess outcomes and enables crosstalk between traditional systems and 
modern medicine through a common interface could increase individuals' health and disease management options and 
provide affordable healthcare solutions. At the Transdisciplinary Centre of Excellence in AI-based Precision Healthcare a 
Centre of Excellence in AyurTech supported by the Ministry of AYUSH has been recently established. Through this 
center, we aim to create a first-of-its-kind unique initiative of combining Functional Genomics, Nanotechnology, 
Electronics, Digital health, and AI for realizing Evidence based Ayurveda solutions. This has the participation of 
collaborators from JCKIC network institutions Dr. SR Rajasthan Ayurved University Jodhpur and AIIMS Jodhpur. This is 
a transdisciplinary program that also have the participation of faculty from diverse engineering sciences from IIT Jodhpur 
which includes Bioscience and Bioengineering, computer science and engineering, electrical engineering, and 
chemistry.This is a unique initiative combining electronics, Digital health and AI & Multiomic technologies for realizing 
“Evidence based Ayurveda'' solutions. The broad objectives of the CoE-AyurTech include four thematic areas and 
capacity building as an integrative approach are described below-

Projects have been initiated in the following areas:
•
Digital devices integrated with IoT, AI and computer vision for rapid, objective and accurate assessments of 
Ayurveda parameters and tailoring interventions
•
Blockchain powered highly secure and privacy preserving smart phone platforms, for large scale Ayurveda 
parameter screening, health and intervention monitoring
•
Laboratory and Point-of-Care (PoC) deployable sensors/ devices, systems
•
Frameworks for Ayurveda drug standardization
•
Open source platforms of drug-disease networks using a compendium of molecular signatures of drugs, 
medicinal plants and Ayurveda based formulations for discoveries, poly-pharmacology and repurposing.
•
Ontological frameworks based on Natural Language Processing for integration of the knowledge base of 
Ayurveda with contemporary terminologies and description.
Ayurtech Centre of Excellence has been established in a built-up space of ~ 3760 sqft. This houses labs for clinical 
and computer vision-based phenotyping, molecular laboratory facilities that include cell and bacterial culture, 
chemistry wet lab, and a device fabrication & characterization area. It also has a setup for conducting training 
workshops besides office spaces. The Center was inaugurated on May 12th, 2023 by Vaidya Rajesh Kotecha, 
Secretary, Ministry of AYUSH, Govt of India. 
Besides leveraging the setups across different departments and the central instrumentation facilities, the Ayurtech 
CoE houses some of the state-of-the-art equipment such as a Table-top Raman Spectrometer, Central accelerated 
computing cluster and extended storage, RF/DC Sputtering System and Dynamic Light Scattering systems.
Highlights
Phenotyping 
and 
Diagnostic 
solutions: 
Computer 
vision-based 
Prakriti 
assessment:
Automatic Prakriti classification requires semantically segmenting the face into various visual attributes such as 
regions corresponding to eyes, nose, eyebrows, teeth, cheeks, lips, forehead, and hair regions. For this purpose, we 
have developed an AI based mechanism that automatically segments these regions given the face’s color image of a 
person. The group is developing a learning-based approach for extracting various features such as color, texture and 
geometry for each of the visual attributes and then classifying the Prakriti using these features followed by the 
allometric scaling to further enhance Prakriti classification. The training data is being created through the 
engagement of volunteers who are being clinically assessed for Prakriti by expert Ayurvedic physicians. A series of 
workshops, training and community engagement sessions have been conducted for participation and objective 
assessment of Prakriti. In-house developed Prakriti Assessment App that could be used with mobile devices are 
being used in the studies.
Development of sensors for objective assessment of biomolecules from body fluids in Prakriti and Vikriti 
conditions: In order to establish the objectivity in diagnostics and therapeutic solutions, various types of sensors are 
being fabricated. These are being developed for detection of biomolecules in sweat, saliva and breath in a more 
objective, precise and quantifiable manner. The ongoing progress for sweat-based nanosensors using silver 
nanoparticles is based on the Surface Enhanced Raman Spectroscopy (SERS) technique in which the detection of 
glucose, ascorbic acid and uric acid has been carried out in the artificially synthesized sweat solution. On the other 
hand, interdigitated electrodes have been fabricated using maskless photolithography techniques for non-enzymatic 
glucose sensing applications. We have also successfully completed the initial design phase for the integrated 
microheater for breath sensing.
Big Data Analytics: Human Phenotype Ontology:
Design of Knowledge graph for mapping phenotypes of Prakriti subtypes to modern medical terminologies and 
other ontological descriptions has been initiated. Also an extensive exercise has been conducted to bridge the 
ontological gap between Ayurveda and Modern Medicine through unifying phenotype terminologies. 
Ayurveda describes diseases from a system’s perspective and has an extensive documentation of phenotypes 
from dosha perspective. The bridging of Ayurveda phenotypes with modern diseases is being attempted 
using human phenotype ontologies and NLP. A set of 10,000 human phenotypes that have been annotated with 
Ayurveda labels are being used to establish linkages between the systems. A graph-database is being designed 
to store all the information about Vikars, HPOs, Diseases and Genes. This database will be connected to the HPO 
ontology. It can connect to other ontologies as well. A front-end visualization and querying platform is being 
envisaged to help in the interoperability of modern and Indian traditional medicine systems.
Development of a participatory platform: 
In our quest to merge tradition with technology, we have designed an Ayurveda Prakriti app that 
intricately weaves ancient Ayurvedic wisdom into the fabric of modern life. The app would enable each user 
to have a personalized health journey, through a comprehensive questionnaire designed to unravel their 
mind-body constitution. The algorithm meticulously computes the percentages and provides users with 
insights into their unique Ayurvedic profile that could guide wellness and disease management.

Therapeutics Technology Solutions: Development of Assay systems and platforms for understanding 
mechanistic basis of ayurvedic formulations: Methods are being developed to characterize and understand the 
mechanisms of action of ayurveda formulations. These are being tested and validated in microbial biofilms, 
cellular and disease models. A transdisciplinary approach involving cellular and structural biology, 
nanotechnology, genomics and chemistry has been undertaken. We intend to develop an Ayurtech framework in 
models that recapitulate metabolic dysfunctions described as “Prameha'' in Ayurveda. Research is ongoing to find 
therapeutic leads from antibacterial Ayurvedic formulas, using structure-guided approaches. The crystal structure 
of the SuhB protein from Pseudomonas aeruginosa, a bacterium linked to diabetic foot ulcers, has been 
resolved to a high precision. This protein, which influences biofilm formation, is a target for developing 
new antimicrobials. Additionally, a pharmacophore based approach is being undertaken to analyse the 
polypharmacological mechanism of Ayush 64, an Ayurvedic remedy that has been effective for mild to 
moderate COVID-19. Lead identification and synthesis of bioactive molecules such as flavonoids and indole 
alkaloids are in progress. Experiments with dosha specific Ayurvedic formulations like vijaysar have shown 
promise against Gram-positive bacteria, particularly in biofilm remodeling, although it hasn’t effectively 
suppressed amyloid formation in biofilms. The cytotoxic effects of Methi, Gurmar, and Vijaysar were assessed 
in both mouse fibroblast and lung cancer cells, revealing that Methi and Gurmar are more potent than Vijaysar. 
A study has also been undertaken to characterise Swarna Bhasma, an Ayurvedic preparation containing gold. 
This formulation shows distinct spectral properties depending on its composition, which were also 
compared to lab-prepared gold seeds. These preliminary studies indicate that Swarna Bhasma might 
contain nano- and micron-sized aggregates. However, detailed studies will further explore the properties and 
potential health benefits of these traditional drugs.

SCHOOL OF MANAGEMENT & ENTREPRENEURSHIP (SME)
The School of Management & Entrepreneurship (SME) is a forward-looking initiative to create and deliver a novel value 
proposition in the management and entrepreneurship education sector in India. Underlying this bold step is the stark 
realization that on account of fast-paced technological changes, the era of stable paradigms in the industry which could be 
exploited through traditional business models, has come to an end. The future will belong to those who are comfortable 
with technologically-dynamic business models, derived from continual expression of entrepreneurial energy exhibited by 
organizational members.
To this end, SME has created an MBA program which integrates technology, management and entrepreneurship through 
an institutional framework which leverages various engineering disciplines, interdisciplinary programs, its own 
innovation and incubation center, and school of liberal arts, apart from management faculties.
Key Highlights
•
48 practitioner sessions as part of the courses
•
23 students doing live projects in start-ups
•
Minimum, Average, Median, Maximum salary package offered (in lakhs): Median: 10.25, Average: 10.91, Max: 25.11
•
30 new recruiters were onboarded in the year
•
33 industry talks/leadership talks organized by SME
Assistant Professors - 10 
 
Associate Professors – 05
Adjunct & Affiliated Faculty - 01 
Administrative Staff - 06
Academic Programs:
MBA Technology / MBA
It is a flagship two year MBA program leading to:
•
Track I – Leading to MBA-Technology Degree
•
Track II – Leading to MBA Degree
•
Track III – Dual Degree (SME, IIT Jodhpur has tie-ups with some of the leading business schools in the world and
jointly offers dual degree programs. The students would successfully complete their foundational courses in the 1st
year at SME, IIT Jodhpur, and thereon would study specialized Master’s degree offerings in the 2nd Year at one of the
partner B-School abroad. The students would go to earn an MBA/MBA-Technology degree from IIT Jodhpur and a
specialized Master’s degree from the partner B-School).
PhD Program
The PhD program at SME is rigorous and demanding. It has been designed to produce candidates with skills and 
achievements, enabling them to meaningfully shape their career for full-time faculty positions in premier management 
institutes across the country.
The PhD program currently provides an opportunity for focused research in all areas of specialization that the school 
offers. The program emphasizes pursuing research work that connects with the world of practice, with any of the national 
or global programs that speak to contemporary issues in our society and their management, particularly those that have an 
overlay of technology and entrepreneurship.
Minor Programs
The undergraduate students at IITJ are offered minor programs to complement their Majors. The minor program must be 
completed simultaneously with a major degree program.
Students can opt for:
•
Minor in Management
•
Minor in Entrepreneurship

Additional information
The entrepreneurial activity development strategy encompasses five interconnected initiatives:
•
Active TISC Engagement: The school prioritizes active engagement with Technology Innovation and Start-up Center at
IIT Jodhpur. This engagement creates formal connection between the school's entrepreneurship education and the
institution's start-up infrastructure, facilitating practical implementation of entrepreneurial concepts taught in
academic programs.
•
Design Credit Utilization: Design Credits, pursued by B. Tech. students are also being utilized to support
entrepreneurial ideation and development. In the recent past, three specific venture projects supported through this
mechanism are:
▪
Mazdoor Mitra: A platform addressing labor market inefficiencies
▪
Agen AI: An artificial intelligence application
▪
Wealth Sync: A wealth management solution
The entrepreneurial activity development strategy demonstrates a comprehensive approach to fostering venture creation 
and innovation skills. By integrating entrepreneurial activities into the curriculum, providing structured support 
mechanisms, and recognizing achievement through competitions and awards, the school creates a supportive ecosystem for 
entrepreneurial development that aligns with its strategic mission and vision.

School of Liberal Arts ( SoLA)

School of Liberal Arts (SoLA)
Department of Humanities and Social Sciences, IITJ evolved into the School of Liberal Arts in June 2022. The change in 
name signifies a change in orientation: The newly established School promotes the idea of transformation by breaking the 
traditional silos between disciplines through multi-, trans-, and interdisciplinary means to strengthen the existing 
research ecosystem.
Vision of the School: The vision of the School is to emerge as a forerunner in Liberal Arts education with a novel, open, 
futuristic, transdisciplinary, and inclusive liberal humanist approach. School of Liberal Arts seeks to engage not only 
with the human, the non-human, and the planetary, but also to recognize and amplify the diverse possibilities and 
potentials of human-technology interfaces as both agents and sites for social change.
Mission of the School: School of Liberal Arts has been founded on the principle that quality education in the Liberal Arts 
is a primary requisite for solving the multidimensional challenges that our current and future generations face. The 
programs are intended to address societal and environmental concerns in transdisciplinary ways.
Academic Programs:
Undergraduate Program: School of Liberal Arts offers several courses for undergraduate students.
•
Compulsory Non-Graded Courses for BTech Students

Professional Communication I and II for all first-year B.Tech. programme

Professional Ethics I and II for all B.Tech. programme


•


Preparatory English I

Preparatory English II
•
Streamwise List of Bouquet Courses

SoLA offers a diversity of courses from various social science and humanities disciplines for BTech
students from their IV to VII semesters.
Post-Graduate Programme:
MSc in Computational Social Science (MSc. CSS), which commenced in July 2022, is the flagship program of the School 
of Liberal Arts, IITJ. The program seeks to develop highly skilled graduates equipped with theoretical, technical, and 
application-oriented knowledge who can construct, improve, analyze and apply theoretically informed models to 
understand processes and phenomena.
Doctoral Programme
School of Liberal Arts also offers a PhD Programme in diverse disciplines including Philosophy, Psychology, Sociology, 
Film Studies, Literary Studies, Linguistics, Cultural Studies, Public Health, and other interdisciplinary areas.
Thrust Research Areas
The school’s research areas are grouped under the following thrust areas: Economics, Psychology, History, Rural 
Development, Public Health, Sociology, Public Policy, Literature, Linguistics, and Culture Studies Visual and 
Performing Arts, Philosophy, Indian Knowledge Systems

New laboratory facilities developed during the Financial Year
Behavioral Science Laboratory
A Behavioral Science Lab is a research facility designed to study human behavior and psychological processes through 
controlled experiments and real-world observations. It combines insights from psychology, economics, neuroscience, 
philosophy, and sociology to understand how people think, feel, and act in different situations. The MoU with the Rekhi 
Foundation has finalized, which will financially support the Happiness research initiative.
Anupama Mohan
•
received World Congress of Environmental History Conference Grant, Oulu, Finland, 2024
•
Anupama Mohan- Landhaus Fellow, Rachel Carson Centre for Environment and Society, 2024
The studio located in W19 is a dedicated space for conducting practical sessions across all Visual and Performing 
Arts courses. In addition to serving academic needs, the studio also supports research activities in the areas of Digital 
Art, New Media, Artistic Practice, and Artist Residencies. The lab is fully equipped with essential infrastructure, 
including tables, chairs, display boards, a projector, music systems, computer systems, and a wide range of art 
supplies, enabling a comprehensive and immersive creative environment.
Sleep 
Cognitive 
and 
Neuromodulation 
Research 
Lab 
(SomnoCore)
The Somno Core Lab is dedicated to cutting-edge research in Sleep and Neuromodulation, pioneering studies to 
enhance brain adaptability, sleep quality, and cognitive health. Equipped with real-time sleep data recording using 
polysomnography and actigraphy, the lab also features workstations for behavioral experiments and 
Neuromodulation research using binaural beats, TMS, and tDCS. By integrating state-of-the-art methodologies, we 
aim to develop transformative solutions that foster brain health, ultimately promoting a more resilient and healthier 
society through innovative, evidence-based Interventions.

Educational institutions and policymakers around the globe have begun to embrace immersive teaching-learning 
technologies that will enable most students to attain optimal educational achievement levels. The Education Technology 
vertical of IIT Jodhpur was set up under the Centre for Emerging Technologies for Sustainable Development (CETSD) in 
2021 to work towards research and delivery, services and training, and social outreach in the area of education technology 
and educational innovation. In October 2022, the vertical was expanded as the Centre for Education & Technology for 
Education (CETE). 
The scope of the this Center includes pedagogical innovation in blended and hybrid education, professional 
development, technology development for teaching-learning needs, and instructional design. The Center has started its 
PhD program from July 2023 and is coordinating the Integrated Teacher Education Program (ITEP) since July 2024.
Academic Programs:
•
PhD Program; Integrated Teacher Education Program
Thematic/Thrust Research Areas:
•
Technology-enhanced learning, blended learning, gamification and game-based learning, behavioral studies,
education policy, learning analytics, teacher education.

New Laboratory Facilities:
•
The EdTech Lab is designed to offer a world-class, hands-on learning environment in e-learning design and
educational technology development. Tailored especially for ITEP and PhD students, the lab is equipped with a smart
interactive panel, high-performance computers, pen tablets, essential software, providing a comprehensive setup for
cutting-edge EdTech education.
•
E-learning Studio (W20), equipped with e-learning authoring tools, editing software, content creation, digital
learning and interaction tools
•
The Physics Pedagogy Lab (situated in Room 220, Department of Physics) has been set up to drive the core
pedagogical training in secondary stage Physics Education for our ITEP program. The lab contains several small-scale
equipment created by Indian Association of Physics Teachers (IAPT). The lab includes thirty-seven hands-on
experiments to demonstrate concepts of kinematics, mechanics, electricity, magnetism, waves and optics. Some of
these are listed below.
Events Organized:
•
Orientation Program for the ITEP Batch of 2024 (03 September 2024)
•
5-Day STEM Teacher Training Program for Jawahar Navodaya Vidyalayas (04 - 08 December 2024). The need for
STEM teacher training is vital to equip educators with skills to foster critical thinking and innovation in students,
aligning with emphasis on experiential and interdisciplinary learning outlined in theNational Education Policy
(NEP) 2020. The 5-day STEM Training Program for PM SHRI Jawahar Navodaya Vidyalaya (JNV) was organized by
Center for Education & Technology for Education (CETE), IIT Jodhpur and Navodaya Leadership Institute, Udaipur
during 04 - 08 December 2024 at IIT Jodhpur. The training program was attended by 56 Teachers from JNVs from
Rajasthan, Haryana, and New Delhi. The Program focused on competency-based science education,
technology-enhanced learning, experiential learning and holistic development of teachers and learners. The 30-hour
program spread across 5 days included interactive sessions, hands-on activities, and lab visits and demonstrations for
the teachers. Fourteen resource persons conducted sessions ranging from competency-based education in science to
edtech tools and e-learning content creation and social-emotional learning.

Centre for Emerging Technologies & 
Sustainable Development (CETSD)
The Center for Emerging Technologies for Sustainable Development (CETSD) came into existence on 14 January 2020. 
CETSD aspires to sustainable development towards a carbon-neutral, bio-based, self-sufficient economy by employing 
exponential, safer and green technologies. The research at CETSD revolves around United Nation Sustainable 
Development Goals (UNSDGs) and subgoals.
Vision: To be a partner in tapping the potential of emerging technologies for creating a sustainable and prosperous future 
India.
Academic Programs 
•
PhD - 25 (2023 onards)
•
MS by Research - 4 (2024 onwards)
•
B.Tech Design Credit - 30 Completed few and some Ongoing

Health Nexus, Geo-Spatial Aspects

STAFF MEMBERS
Administrative Staff - 01
The Center for Technology Foresight and Policy (CTFP) came into existence at IIT Jodhpur in January 2020. The vision of 
CTFP is “Foresight Advocacy for Technology and Policy Impact.” The center focuses on foresight and evolving areas of 
technology to provide future roadmaps and policy recommendations. The center also promotes foresight and its 
methodologies in the public and private sectors. 
The CTFP is dedicated to exploring future trends, emerging technologies, and strategic developments to project plausible 
futures. Our work is grounded in foresight methodology, a structured approach to anticipating and preparing for future 
challenges and opportunities. We promote foresight as a capability that can be developed both at the individual and 
organizational levels. The CTFP has been in discussions with organizations such as the Technology Information, 
Forecasting and Assessment Council (TIFAC), the National Center of Good Governance (NCGG), and Central Detective 
Training Institute, Jaipur (part of BPR&D).
This can be achieved by both focused initiatives and human capital and knowledge development. In an era of rapid 
technological evolution and geopolitical uncertainty, foresight enables proactive decision-making rather than reactive 
responses. It helps institutions mitigate risks, seize opportunities, and build adaptive strategies to navigate complex 
futures. The CTFP also plans to become a hub for futuristic strategy and policy think tanks.
Information on Academic Programs hosted:
•
CTFP offers MS (Research) and PhD in foresight.
Thematic/Thrust Research Areas:
Indicative topics emanating from current activities include Technology Assessment, Pathways and Forecasting, Foresight 
Methods, Evidence-based Policy Analysis, Life Cycle Assessment, Policy Design for Governing Complex Socio-Technical 
Systems, Design of Emerging Technology-based Information Systems (ETIS), Future of Policy Making, Foresight-driven 
Policy Making, Foresight-based Sustainability, and Foresight-based Corporate Governance. Specific technologies of 
interest within the Center include Artificial Intelligence (AI), Internet of Things (IoT), Blockchain, Quantum Technologies, 
and Decarbonisation technologies. Specific application domains of interest include Logistics, Transportation, and Energy.
Research Highlights:
The CTFP is dedicated to exploring future trends, emerging technologies, and strategic developments to project plausible 
futures. Our work is grounded in foresight methodology, a structured approach to anticipating and preparing for future 
challenges and opportunities. We promote foresight as a capability that can be developed both at the individual and 
organizational levels. The CTFP has been in discussions with organizations such as the Technology Information, 
Forecasting and Assessment Council (TIFAC), the National Center of Good Governance (NCGG), and Central Detective 
Training Institute, Jaipur (part of BPR&D).

Center for Technology Foresight and Policy (CTFP) Project

SECTION 8

Technology Innovation & Start-up Centre (TISC)
The Technology Innovation and Start-up Centre (TISC) at IIT Jodhpur, a Section 8 company, has continued to strengthen 
its role as a catalyst for innovation, entrepreneurship, and translational research during the financial year 2024–25. 
This year was marked by significant ecosystem engagements, impactful programs, and collaborative partnerships 
aimed at supporting early-stage ventures and academic integration.
TISC supports the incubation and pre-incubation of 51 start-ups spanning domains such as digital health, deep tech, 
med-tech, clean tech, and educational technologies. The incubation portfolio benefitted from national-level programs 
including BioNEST (supported by BIRAC) and the MSME IDEA Hackathon 3.0. Additionally, several initiatives 
enhanced cross-disciplinary engagement and capacity building within and beyond the institute.
Nine batches of the MIT-WPU National Academic Immersion Program (NAIP) were successfully conducted in 
collaboration with various academic departments, fostering interdisciplinary learning and academic enrichment among 
students.
A wide range of flagship programs were hosted by TISC during the year:
A one-day BIRAC Sensitization Program on Bio-Entrepreneurship and Intellectual Property & Technology Management 
was conducted to promote awareness on IP strategy and bio-enterprise development.
The Green FinTech Hackathon 2024, organized in association with the Reserve Bank Innovation Hub (RBIH), catalyzed 
innovation at the intersection of finance and sustainability, encouraging green finance solutions from early-stage 
startups and student innovators.
A DST-supported deep-tech identification program, in collaboration with GDC-IIT Madras, aimed to identify and 
mentor startups emerging from STEM research with high commercialization potential.
TISC also organized the DST-NIDHI – C-CAMP Accelerator Programme, providing early-stage deep-tech and life 
science startups access to critical mentoring and scale-up support.
A one-day workshop-cum-orientation program was conducted at Madhav University on emerging technologies like 
Machine Learning (ML), Deep Learning (DL), Natural Language Processing (NLP), and the Internet of Things (IoT), 
expanding TISC’s outreach in regional academic ecosystems.
In addition, Biz-Kidz, a flagship youth entrepreneurship event, was organized as part of Utsav 2025, promoting 
entrepreneurial thinking among school students in a fun and engaging format.
TISC also deepened institutional partnerships with organizations such as FITT-IIT Delhi, SIIC-IIT Kanpur, Unicorn 
Incubator Korea, and the Reserve Bank Innovation Hub, while continuing to offer IP, legal, and grant-writing support 
to innovators across the IITJ ecosystem.
Overall, FY 2024–25 has been a year of impactful programs, strengthened partnerships, and increased outreach, 
positioning TISC as a key driver of IIT Jodhpur’s innovation and entrepreneurship vision.
Jodhpur City Knowledge & Innovation Foundation (JCKIF)
Jodhpur City Knowledge and Innovation Foundation (JCKIF), is a Section-8 company (Non-Profit Organization) 
established on 31st March, 2021 under the Companies Act 2013 to carry out and sustain the activities of Jodhpur City 
Knowledge and Innovation Cluster (JCKIC).
JCKIC is an initiative of the Office of the Principal Scientific Adviser (PSA) to the Government of India on the 
recommendation of the Prime Minister’s Science, Technology and Innovation Advisory Council (PM-STIAC) to create 
an Atmanirbhar Bharat through Science & Technology. Indian Institute of Technology Jodhpur (IITJ) is nodal agency for 
JCKIC.
JCKIF acts as a facilitator for Jodhpur Cluster to create strong linkages among major Academic Institutions, R & D 
Institutes, National & State Research Laboratories, Government Agencies and Industries of the city of Jodhpur and
surroundings. In 2024, JCKIF received ₹5 crore in second-phase funding to strengthen three key verticals: Handicrafts 
& Handlooms, Medical Technologies, and Rainwater Harvesting & Conservation. In the Handicrafts & Handlooms 
sector, JCKIF launched Kalaanubhav.in, a digital platform showcasing over 800 artisan products, and set up a 3D 
Experience Center at IIT Jodhpur. JCKIF also facilitated 19 design registrations and initiated GI tagging for the Sindhi 
Sarangi, in addition to co-organizing THRIVE 2025, a national summit on sustainable innovation. In Medical 
Technologies, JCKIF co-hosted ICMI 2025, a national conference held from February 15–17, 2025. In the area of 
Rainwater Harvesting & Conservation, it launched the SEIP 2025 Internship Program to encourage student-led projects 
in water sustainability. Through these initiatives, JCKIF continues to drive impactful, science-led development across 
the region.The Rural Electrification Corporation Foundation sanctioned a Rs 1,52 crore CSR project to provide school 
supplies to 41 childcare institutions. AIOT-IHF, a joint venture with RajCOMP and IIT Jodhpur, has a Rs 190 crore 
budget.

TIH-iHub Drishti Foundation, 
IIT Jodhpur
The IIT Jodhpur’s Technology Innovation Hub, known as iHub Drishti, is dedicated to the development of cyber-
physical systems that encompass Computer Vision (CV), Augmented Reality (AR), and Virtual Reality (VR). This 
hub operates as a non-profit organisation, registered under Section-8, and was established as part of the 
National Mission on Interdisciplinary Cyber-Physical Systems (NM-ICPS), which is an initiative of the 
Government of India. These focus areas will drive technological advancements in applications such as: (i) 
Computer Vision for Autonomous Systems, (ii) Computer Vision for Healthcare and Biosphere, (iii) Imaging for 
Document Analysis, (iv) CV and VR for Industry 4.0, and (v) Dependable AR/VR for X.
Under Computer Vision for Autonomous Systems, iHub Drishti is also involved in developing Autonomous 
Systems for robots that can perceive their environment in indoor and outdoor settings. Under Computer Vision 
for Healthcare and Biosphere, iHub Drishti offers Vision-Based Solutions for healthcare, including (i) CV-based 
chronic Diabetic Wound Healing Management, (ii) Hub for Radiogenomics and Services, Non-invasive 
Diagnosis of Coronary Artery Disease using miRNA and Coronary Imaging, (iii) AI-based risk stratification 
referral models, (iv) using eye images in a public health setting, (v) Evaluation and development of Machine 
Learning (ML) models for the automated detection, (vi) localisation and characterisation of traumatic rib 
fractures on CT scans. The hub has demonstrated a robust capacity for impactful translational work. Signature 
initiatives include “Campus Rakshak” for pandemic management, AR/VR frameworks for heritage and 
medical training, and real-time 3D scene reconstruction for defense and autonomous navigation. 
Technologies like the “TrustMe” platform for adversarial attack detection and the “Vadnagar Heritage 
Game” reflect the hub’s blend of scientific innovation and societal relevance. Through its strategic 
collaborations with institutions like DRDO, NSF, AIIMS, and various IITs, iHub Drishti has also facilitated 
international projects and field-deployable prototypes, many of which have led to commercialization or are 
currently being incubated as start-ups. Start-ups such as Oncosphera Pvt. Ltd., Cellverse Pvt. Ltd. demonstrate 
how academic research has transitioned into entrepreneurial ventures with real-world impact. Dependable AR/
VR for X, iHub Drishti has established advanced labs, such as the Omniverse Nucleus for Mixed Reality Lab and 
Digital Gaming Lab. These labs feature high-end technology, including NVIDIA A40 GPU and Intel Xeon 
Processor. Key features include real-time simulation, AI integration, remote collaboration, and customisation 
through the Omniverse Kit. The labs also incorporate Omniverse Holodeck for immersive simulations, 
making them ideal for testing, training, and exploration across various fields. This technology is a valuable asset 
for real-time 3D content creation and collaboration across sectors. iHub Drishti also contributes to several 
innovative programmes of IIT Jodhpur, including the MTech AR/VR in collaboration with the School of 
Artificial Intelligence and Data Science (SAIDE), IITJ, Masters in XR Design in collaboration with the School of 
Liberal Arts (SoLA), and the Samsung Certification programme for Samsung employees focusing on 
Advanced Computer Vision and Graphics.
STARTUPS SUPPORTED & IPRs FILED 
The iHub Drishti Foundation has provided Promotion and Acceleration of Young and Aspiring 
Technology Entrepreneurs (PRAYAS) and Seed-Support to 10 startups (Cellverse, Oncosphera, Novealthy 
Innovation, Unicorniz Innovations, SVAR, POZE Analytics, Ripple Healthcare, Altie Reality, Sparshmind 
Innovations and Edumeasy). iHub Drishti Foundation has filed the following 16 Intellectual Properties (IPs), 
including Patents, Copyright, Trademark and Design Applications.
COLLABORATIONS/MOU’S 
iHub Drishti has emerged as a pivotal organization fostering cross-disciplinary innovation through its extensive 
network of collaborations with academic, research, and industrial partners. The foundation has signed 
MoUs and research agreements with premier institutions such as AIIMS Rishikesh, VIT Vellore, BIT 
Mesra Jaipur, IIIT Bangalore, NIMHANS, and international bodies like the US National Science Foundation. 
Additionally, collaboration with IGNCA, New Delhi, has driven the digitization of ancient manuscripts. 
Furthermore, iHub Drishti has organized skilling programs, including M.Tech executive and Winter Schools, 
hosting experts from premier institutions worldwide. These collective efforts not only demonstrate a multi-
sectoral engagement model but also position iHub Drishti as a catalyst in bridging academia, industry, and society 
for technology-driven development.

RECENT OUTREACH ACTIVITIES 
iHub Drishti Foundation played a significant role in several prominent national-level academic events in 2024. Notably, 
they sponsored the 9th National Conference on Computer Vision, Pattern Recognition, Image Processing, and Graphics 
(NCVPRIPG 2024) held at IIST Trivandrum, drawing 200 participants from various technical disciplines. They also 
organized the Winter School on AI and Theoretical Computer Science at IIT Jodhpur, which focused on the latest 
developments in generative AI models and hosted 106 attendees. Additionally, the foundation sponsored and exhibited 
at ROSCon India 2024 hosted at IISc Bangalore, a key event in the robotics community, with 400 attendees, and 
supported ICVGIP 2024 at IIIT-Bangalore and CVIP 2024 at IIITDM Kancheepuram, both essential platforms in 
computer vision and graphics. On the international front, iHub Drishti demonstrated global outreach by sponsoring and 
co-hosting high-impact events. This included the International Workshop on Big Data in Healthcare (BDH 2024), held as 
part of IEEE MIPR in San Jose, USA, with a targeted audience of 50 researchers and practitioners.
IIT Jodhpur Marudhara Foundation
The IIT Jodhpur Marudhara Foundation is dedicated to promoting education, research, and other academic activities at 
IIT Jodhpur. The foundation received INR 65.1 lakhs in 2024 as CSR contributions and donations. The foundation also 
established a merit prize and a memorial award to recognize student achievements.
Research & Technology Park
The IIT Jodhpur Technology Park, incorporated in 2019 as a Section 8 not-for-profit company promoted by the Institute, 
has made substantial progress this year. With all operational mechanisms now in place, 2024–25 marks the formal 
commencement of activities at the TechPark. This initiative is an important milestone in IIT Jodhpur’s journey toward 
deepening its engagement with industry, fostering translational research, and facilitating innovation that addresses 
pressing national and regional challenges.
The Technology Park has been envisioned as a platform that enables seamless integration between academia and 
industry. It provides a collaborative environment to co-develop technologies, jointly create intellectual property, and 
enable faster translation of research outcomes into real-world solutions.
Purpose and Scope
The establishment of a Technology Park within the IIT Jodhpur campus serves multiple strategic objectives. For the 
Institute, it opens new pathways for industry-funded research, enhances experiential learning opportunities for 
students, and builds a stronger innovation culture. For industry partners, it offers direct access to high-end research 
infrastructure, cutting-edge ideas, and a talented pool of faculty and students. For the region, it promises local high-skill 
job creation, deployment of context-sensitive technologies, and development of entrepreneurship hubs in Western 
Rajasthan.
The Park is designed to support the entire innovation lifecycle—from ideation and prototyping to pilot deployment and 
commercialization—thus creating an end-to-end ecosystem for applied research and industrial collaboration.
Objectives
The key objectives of the IIT Jodhpur Technology Park are:
•
To establish a world-class, interdisciplinary R&D ecosystem that nurtures both academic excellence and industry
relevance.
•
To forge long-term academia–industry partnerships that go beyond funding, involving co-development of
technologies, joint IP ownership, and collaborative research centres.
•
To facilitate technology translation by enabling rapid prototyping, validation, and field deployment of
research-driven solutions.
To align with national missions in areas such as cybersecurity, clean energy, digital health, water sustainability, and 
preservation of cultural heritage.
Industry Engagement Models
To facilitate flexible engagement, the Technology Park has established two industry partnership models:
Resident Members: These partners establish a physical presence within the Park, with access to office space, laboratories, 
and testing facilities. This model is suited for companies seeking continuous engagement with faculty and infrastructure 
to support R&D or product co-creation.

Affiliate Members: These partners engage with the Institute in a virtual or hybrid mode. They participate in all the 
activities such as joint research initiatives, special-interest groups (SIGs), faculty roundtables, student projects, and 
limited facility access, without maintaining a full-time campus presence.
This dual-model framework enables broad-based industry participation, ranging from large corporations to start-ups 
and policy organisations.
Special Interest Groups (SIGs)
As part of the Park’s operational strategy, Special Interest Groups (SIGs) are being formed in thematic areas aligned 
with IIT Jodhpur’s research strengths and national priorities. These SIGs aim to bring together faculty members and 
industry representatives to explore collaborative opportunities and build a focused research agenda. The focus areas 
of the SIGs include but are not limited to:
•
Artificial Intelligence and Data Science (AI & DS)
•
Robotics and Autonomous Systems
•
Computer Vision and Natural Language Understanding
•
Extended Reality (AR/VR) and Human–Machine Interaction (HMI)
•
Clean and Green Energy
•
Digital Health and Biomedical Devices
•
Water and Environmental Sustainability
•
Culture and Heritage Technologies
Key Activities in 2024–25
1. Infrastructure Allocation: IITJ Technology Park has 3800 sq. ft. of space in the form of shared offices, in addition to
common facilities such as meeting rooms and innovation labs.
2. Round Tables with Faculty: The Technology Park organized multiple round-table discussions with faculty members
to understand the major research themes and areas of faculty members.
3. Industry Visits: The team conducted visits to research parks at other IITs and interacted with other industries. These
visits provided insights into operational best practices, funding strategies, and collaborations.
Industry Partners
The following organisations have been associated with the Technology Park:
The 2024–25 academic year marked the beginning of operational activities for the IIT Jodhpur Technology Park. From 
establishing processes to activating SIGs, the Park has laid a strong foundation for integrated industry–academia 
collaboration. Moving forward, the focus will be on expanding engagement, enabling joint R&D outputs, and 
strengthening the institute’s contribution to innovation-led development in India. The Park exemplifies IIT Jodhpur’s 
vision of being a catalyst for technological advancement, regional upliftment, and national impact.

Planning and Resource Generation
The Office of Resource Generation at the Institute plays a pivotal role in mobilizing financial resources from a 
diverse range of stakeholders, including industries, philanthropic foundations, individual donors, and the 
global alumni community. Leveraging the Institute’s registration under the Corporate Social Responsibility 
(CSR) framework, the office is empowered to seek and secure contributions from corporate entities and 
charitable organizations to support a wide spectrum of academic, research, infrastructural, and developmental 
initiatives.
In its mission to foster meaningful partnerships, the Office of Resources & Alumni curates and facilitates a 
variety of strategic programs and engagement activities. These initiatives are designed to create dynamic 
platforms for interaction and collaboration between industry leaders, corporate representatives, faculty 
members, students, and staff of IIT Jodhpur. Through such engagements, the IIT Jodhpur not only strengthens 
institutional ties with external stakeholders but also nurtures a culture of innovation and mutual growth.
Furthermore, the Office of Resources Generation plays an instrumental role in coordinating and managing 
scholarship programs generously sponsored by corporations, philanthropists, and well-wishers. These 
scholarships are vital in supporting meritorious and financially underprivileged students, thereby 
reinforcing the Institute’s commitment to inclusive and accessible education. The donations can also be 
provided for various avenues listed at our IITJ webpage, i.e. https://corel.iitj.ac.in/donation.php

International Relations
IIT Jodhpur is actively advancing internationalization by fostering collaborations with foreign universities 
and institutions in research, development, and academic partnerships. Since its establishment, the Office of 
International Relations (IR) has been instrumental in building global alliances, facilitating the execution of MoUs and 
agreements with international institutions. The IR has also spearheaded proposals for collaboration, offering 
administrative and institutional support to ensure the successful implementation of these partnerships.
Moreover, IIT Jodhpur has welcomed international students from Indonesia, Cambodia, Ethiopia, Syria, Nepal, 
and Bangladesh through various Indian government initiatives such as the ASEAN Fellowship Program, Study in India 
(SII), Indian Council for Cultural Relations (ICCR), Direct Admission Channel, and mutually agreed exchange 
programs with foreign institutes. The institute has forged connections with universities across the globe, including 
the USA, France, Belgium, the Republic of Korea, Russia, Germany, England, Switzerland, Norway, Japan, Morocco, 
and Australia.
The IR also plays a crucial role in coordinating exchange and visiting programs for students, faculty, and researchers, 
promoting collaboration in education and research. Additionally, it facilitates visits from international academic 
and diplomatic delegations while organizing IIT Jodhpur delegations’ trips to foreign universities to strengthen 
existing partnerships and establish new ones. The development and execution of Memorandums of Understanding 
(MoUs) and agreements with partner institutions and organizations are also efficiently managed by the Office of IR.
Details of National and International MoUs facilitated through the Office of International Relations are as below:
International Student Orientation:
For the first time, IIT Jodhpur organized the International Student Orientation Program, spearheaded by the Office of
International Relations, on September 4th, 2024. The event welcomed students from Nepal, Bangladesh, Ethiopia, Syria,
and Indonesia, introducing them to IIT Jodhpur's world-class education, cutting-edge research, and vibrant campus life.
Direct Admission Channel:
In the academic year 2024-25, IIT Jodhpur has introduced a Direct Admission Offer for the top ten graduating
undergraduate and postgraduate international students (stream-wise) from prestigious global universities. This initiative
aims to draw high-caliber international students, enhancing the institute's research ecosystem and expanding its global
footprint.

UK-India Capacity Building Workshop:
The UK-India Capacity Building Workshop, an interdisciplinary initiative jointly organized by IIT Jodhpur and the
University of Birmingham, UK, aims to foster collaborative research between the two nations in sustainable energy
systems. Focusing on key areas such as energy policies, entrepreneurship, innovation, and green finance, the workshop
invites participation from faculty members, undergraduate and postgraduate students, doctoral researchers, and
early-career professionals.

Group Photo of UK-India Capacity Building Workshop
Participation at Heritage Network:
IIT Jodhpur has been selected as the Observer Member of the Heritage Network, and our Institute will be involved in the
forthcoming General Assemblies of the Heritage Network for a duration of four (04) years. The Heritage Network serves
as a platform for India-Europe collaboration in education and research within the field of engineering sciences. On 14th
May 2025, the Office of International Relations presented the progress of IIT Jodhpur’s international initiatives at the
Heritage Network with following objectives:
•
Enhancing Global Collaboration: Establish partnerships with international institutions for joint research projects,
faculty exchanges, and student mobility programs.
•
Advancing Interdisciplinary Research: Utilize our expertise in Robotics and Mobility Systems, Digital Humanities,
Smart Healthcare, IoT and Applications, Quantum Information and Computation, Space Science and Technology, and
more to support the network’s goals.
•
Strengthening Cultural and Educational Connections: Encourage the exchange of ideas, heritage conservation
strategies, and academic best practices among partner institutions.
Proposal of Endowment Funds:
IIT Jodhpur has introduced Endowment funds to support structured models designed for international students enrolling 
in UG, PG, and Ph.D. programs at the Institute. These awards will help cover expenses such as registration fees, tuition 
fees, hostel accommodation, food, and other necessary costs.
Admission Status of Foreign National at IIT Jodhpur
Through extensive global outreach efforts, the Office of International Relations has received around 236 applications via 
the Study in India (SII) and Direct Admission Channel from diverse countries, including Ethiopia, Indonesia, Korea, Nepal, 
Bangladesh, Syria, Uganda and the United States. Following an internal selection process across various 
departments/schools/centers, 40 admission letters have been issued (as on 19th June 2025) for various postgraduate 
courses. Out of which, 12 students have completed their first semester fee payment and are set to begin their postgraduate 
studies at IIT Jodhpur in the upcoming academic session of 2025-26.

B. Inaugural Meet of IITJ- Mumbai Alumni Chapter
The Mumbai Alumni Chapter of IIT Jodhpur held its inaugural meet on January 17, 2025, marking a significant milestone
in alumni engagement. The event was honored by the presence of Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal, Director of IIT Jodhpur,
Prof. Kaushal Desai, Dean of Resources & Alumni, Prof. Shankar Manoharan, Associate Dean of Alumni Relations, Dr.
Ankur Gupta, Associate Dean of International Relations, Mr. Baikuntha Nath Sahu, Assistant Registrar, and Mr. Vaibhav
Gundre, President of the IITJ Alumni Association. Their participation underscored the significance of this event in
strengthening the institute's alumni network and fostering a sense of belonging among graduates.
During the gathering, Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal addressed the alumni on their importance to IIT Jodhpur and urge
them to be connected with the IIT Jodhpur. Prof. Desai addressed the alumni, emphasizing the importance of their
collective contributions to the institute’s growth and future endeavors. The Associate Dean of Alumni Relations
highlighted various initiatives aimed at enhancing engagement between alumni and the institute, and insights into
administrative and networking opportunities available to the alumni community.
Alumni Relations
Alumni are important stakeholders of the Institute. The Alumni of IIT Jodhpur continue to exemplify the values and 
excellence instilled by our institution, consistently achieving noteworthy milestones in their respective domains. Their 
diverse endeavours span over entrepreneurship, academia, corporate leadership, civil services, and beyond, which brings 
the glory and recognition to IIT Jodhpur. Noteworthy successes include ventures such as Kuku FM and Veda Bio, academic 
roles in esteemed institutions like the University of Kansas and the University of California, as well as leadership positions 
at McKinsey, Alpha Advisors, Deutsche Bank, Mercedes Benz, and other corporate leaders.
A glimpse of the initiatives undertaken by the Office of Alumni are presented below:
A. IIT Jodhpur Alumni Day 2025 and Dashak 3.0
The Annual Alumni Day and Dashak 3.0- the decennial reunion for the Class of 2015 was hosted in its sprawling campus
from January 25-26, 2025. The campus community came together to welcome back the alumni, and witnessed active
participation from U.G, P.G. and Ph.D. alumni across various batches. The two days event started with the address by Prof.
Avinash Kumar Agarwal, Director, IIT Jodhpur. Dr. Shankar Manoharan, Associate Dean, Alumni Relations welcomed the
gathering and Prof. Kaushal Desai, Dean of Resources & Alumni, addressed the Alumni on how they can come together to
support the Institute in its mission. Vote of thanks was proposed by Prof. Kaushal A. Desai. All Alumni from the Class of
2015 were felicitated by the Institute during the event.
Continuing with its annual tradition, this year, the Institute has announced the Recognition of Excellence in Young Alumni
(REYA)-2025 Awards in various categories. The following Alumni have been recognized and awarded with the REYA 2025
awards:

C. PIWOT Mumbai Meeting
The PIWOT Global Technology Summit 2025, held from January 17 to January 19, 2025 at the Jio World Convention Centre 
in Mumbai, served as a dynamic platform for industry leaders, innovators, and academic institutions to discuss the 
evolving impact of technology across various sectors.
IIT Jodhpur participated actively in the summit, highlighting its advancements in research and innovation through a 
dedicated booth representation. The event was attended by Prof. Avinash Agarwal, Director of IIT Jodhpur; Prof. Kaushal 
Desai, Dean of Resources & Alumni; Prof. Shankar Manoharan, Associate Dean of Alumni Relations; Prof. Ankur Gupta, 
Associate Dean of International Connect; and Mr. Baikuntha Nath Sahu, Assistant Registrar (Resources & Alumni). Their 
presence reinforced the institute’s commitment to fostering collaborations, engaging with technological advancements, 
and strengthening its network within the global tech community.
IIT Jodhpur participated actively, showcasing its research and innovations through a dedicated booth representation. The 
summit provided a platform for knowledge exchange, fostering collaborations between academia, industry experts, and 
entrepreneurs. Discussions focused on startups, sustainability, and digital transformation, reinforcing IIT Jodhpur’s 
commitment to driving innovation and technological progress. Through networking and engagement, the institute 
strengthened its presence in the global tech ecosystem.

D. Alumni Induction Program
The Office of Alumni Relations organized the Alumni Induction program on 26th October 2024 followed by dinner on the 
occasion of the convocation of the Institute. The event started with the welcome address by Prof. Shankar Manoharan, 
Associate Dean of Alumni Relations . Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal, Director IIT Jodhpur formally inducted around 1084 
graduates as Alumni of the Institute and also congratulated the students and motivated them to connect and work for the 
welfare of the nation. Mr. Vaibhav Gundre, President, IITJ Alumni Association congratulated the graduating students 
and welcomed them into the IITJ Alumni Association. He also highlighted the initiatives of the association and its 
commitment to work with the Institute for mutual benefits. He motivated the graduating class to connect with the 
Alumni excelling in diverse fields by networking through local chapters. The event concluded with a formal vote of 
thanks by Prof. Kaushal Desai, Dean of Resources & Alumni followed by the gala dinner.
E. Key Activities Conducted by Society of Alumni Affairs (SAA)
The Society of Alumni Affairs, in collaboration with the Office of Resources & Alumni, has formally launched LEGACY 
2024-a flagship joint initiative serving as the institution’s annual fundraising campaign. It was dedicated to advancing 
student-centric initiatives. Through LEGACY 2024, the partnership seeks to mobilize the enduring support of alumni and 
benefactors, fostering a culture of giving back to the institute that underscores the shared commitment to nurturing future 
generations.

latest initiatives in fostering meaningful partnerships during the exhibition.

Introduction
The Indian Institute of Technology Jodhpur (IIT Jodhpur) through its Office of Executive Education, continues to expand 
its academic outreach beyond the confines of traditional education. Recognizing the increasing demand for flexible, 
industry-aligned, and future-ready learning pathways, the Office has strategically developed and delivered a robust suite 
of executive and professional education programs.
These offerings are crafted to meet the dynamic needs of working professionals, industry leaders, government 
functionaries, and academic staff—contributing meaningfully to the national agenda of skill development, employment 
generation, and socio-economic progress. The academic year 2024–25 marks another significant milestone in the evolution 
of the Office, characterized by record-breaking enrolment, strategic program expansion, and fruitful industry 
collaborations.
The Office of Executive Education at IIT Jodhpur is committed to:
•
Fostering a culture of lifelong learning
•
Delivering modular and stackable educational offerings
•
Ensuring close alignment with industry demands
•
Bridging the gap between academic theory and practical application
•
Supporting national and international initiatives in upskilling and reskilling
•
Enhancing the institutional reputation and stakeholder engagement
By leveraging a combination of academic excellence, faculty expertise, and strategic partnerships, the Office is shaping 
professionals who are agile, competent, and future-ready.
A hallmark of IIT Jodhpur’s executive education is its stackable program model, which offers tiered credentials at different 
academic milestones:
•
Certificate Level
•
Diploma Level
•
M. Tech Degree
This flexible design accommodates the diverse needs of working professionals by allowing seamless entry, exit, and
re-entry into the academic system—without compromising on academic rigor or institutional standards. It enables
learners to pace their education based on career objectives, personal responsibilities, and evolving industry demands.
Over the past five years, the Office of Executive Education has demonstrated remarkable growth in program offerings 
and student enrolment:
Executive Education Program

This upward trajectory is a testament to the relevance, quality, and responsiveness of the programs offered by IIT Jodhpur 
to meet the needs of an evolving global economy.
Categories of Programs Offered
1. Short-Term Programs
Curated for professionals seeking immediate skill acquisition, these programs target sector-specific competencies. In
2023–24, the Office conducted three such programs, enrolling over 200 participants.
2. Skill Development Programs
These hands-on programs emphasize employability and workforce readiness. IIT Jodhpur conducted two such programs
in 2023–24, enrolling 310 students. Notably, under PMKVY 4.0, 100 participants completed industry-relevant courses
designed and delivered by IIT Jodhpur faculty and industry partners.
3. Executive MTech Programs
A wide range of Executive M. Tech programs were successfully run during the year:
•
Artificial Intelligence
•
Robotics and Mobility Systems
•
Augmented and Virtual Reality
•
Data Engineering
•
Distributed Computing Systems (DCS)
•
Intelligent VLSI Systems (IVS)
Each of these programs integrates real-world applications with foundational theory, offering a unique blend of academic
learning and industry orientation.
4. Postgraduate Diplomas and Certificates
To cater to varied professional interests, the Office offers stackable postgraduate diplomas and certificates:
•
PG Diploma in Data Engineering
•
PG Diploma in Artificial Intelligence
•
PG Diploma in OMICS Technologies and Applications
•
PG Certificate in Machine Learning and AI
•
Certificate Programs in Next-Generation OMICS Technologies
These programs serve as both standalone qualifications and stepping stones toward the Executive M. Tech degree.
5. Undergraduate Online Programs
•
B.Sc./B.S. in Applied AI and Data Science: This innovative online program enables students and professionals to
pursue quality education in emerging technologies from remote locations while maintaining job continuity. This is a
one-of-a-kind programme offered by IIT Jodhpur.
6. Faculty and Staff Development Initiatives
Recognizing the importance of capacity building within the institution, the Office has conducted several specialized
programs for staff and faculty:
•
English for Office Works (Jan–March 2023): 104 participants
•
Training on GeM & GFR (June 2023): 106 participants
•
Human Rights Training in collaboration with NHRC (Dec 2023): 40 participants
•
Pedagogy and Technology-Enabled Learning (FDP)
These initiatives support continuous improvement, policy compliance, and professional development within the
institute’s workforce.
Academic Year No. of Programs Enrolled Students

The Office of Executive Education actively partners with organizations to co-design and deliver contemporary and 
relevant programs:
•
OmicsLogic India (Pine Biotech)
•
Premas Life Sciences Pvt. Ltd.
•
Futurense Technology Pvt. Ltd.
As IIT Jodhpur moves forward, the Office of Executive Education has outlined several strategic objectives:
•
Diversify Executive Offerings: Expansion into domains like quantum computing, cybersecurity, digital health,
climate resilience, and smart infrastructure.
•
Strengthen Industry and Government Partnerships: Forge deeper collaborations with public-sector bodies, private
enterprises, and international universities.
•
Enhance Alumni Engagement: Leverage the professional success of alumni for mentorship, feedback, and program
development.
•
Adopt Global Best Practices: Benchmark programs against leading global executive education models.
The academic year 2024–25 was a transformative period for the Office of Executive Education at IIT Jodhpur. Through 
rapid expansion, quality delivery, and strategic foresight, the Office has made significant strides toward positioning IIT 
Jodhpur as a national hub for lifelong learning and professional advancement. With its people-centric approach, agile 
academic structure, and commitment to excellence, the Office is poised to lead the next generation of executive and 
continuing education in India and beyond.

Academics

Introduction to the activities of the 
Office of Academic Affairs
The Office of Academic Affairs oversees the complete spectrum of academic programs at the Institute, from admission 
planning to convocation. Its responsibilities include admissions to various programs- B.Tech., B.S., B.Sc.-B.Ed. (ITEP), 
M.Tech., M.Sc., M.Sc.-M.Tech., MBA, M.Tech.-Ph.D., Masters, M.Des., M.S. (by Research), Masters-Ph.D., and Ph.D.- based
on national-level examinations such as JEE (Advanced), GATE, JAM, CAT, UGC-NET, CEED, as well as the Institute’s
internal examinations. In addition, the Office manages academic registration, orientation programs, examinations (online
and offline), convocation, and the administration of lecture halls and departmental classrooms.
The Office of Academic Affairs successfully organized the 10th Convocation of the Institute on October 26, 2024. During the
ceremony, a total of 1,084 students were conferred degrees, diplomas, and certificates: 425 B.Tech., 76 M.Sc., 17
M.Sc.-M.Tech., 370 M.Tech., 7 Masters, 48 MBA, 29 MBA-Tech., 87 PG Diploma/Certificate, 1 M.Tech.-Ph.D., and 24 Ph.D.
recipients.
Further, the student strength has witnessed a substantial increase, rising from 4,758 in AY 2023–24 to 6783 in AY 2024–25.
New Initiatives
The Institute has established the following new Academic units:
MedTech. Centre: The Medical Technologies Programs were initiated in 2020 as a joint initiative between the Institute and 
AIIMS Jodhpur. Since their inception, these programs have evolved significantly, with a focus on enhancing healthcare 
quality, accessibility, efficiency, waste reduction, and cost-effectiveness.
India’s healthcare landscape is dynamic, characterized by a pronounced urban–rural divide, an ongoing epidemiological 
transition from communicable to non-communicable diseases, and the challenges of a growing population coupled with 
increasing life expectancy. While medical technologies available to Indian patients are often adapted to local needs, they do 
not always adequately address the diverse and complex healthcare requirements of the country. The rapid advancement of 
technology, scientific discoveries, engineering innovations, and global connectivity offers immense opportunities for the 
development of innovative techniques, devices, and products. The nonlinear pace of technological change is expected to 
disrupt healthcare markets, thereby creating opportunities for both established healthcare organizations and emerging 
start-up enterprises.
In this context, the establishment of a Joint Center for Medical Technologies would act as a catalyst for multi-disciplinary 
collaborations and the development of need-based, cutting-edge healthcare technologies. Such an initiative will require 
professionals with diverse academic backgrounds, along with training in entrepreneurship and business dynamics, to drive 
innovation and ensure effective translation of technologies into clinical practice.
Manekshaw Centre of Excellence for National Security Studies and Research (MCOENSSR) 
at IIT Jodhpur:
IIT Jodhpur has established the Manekshaw Centre of Excellence for National Security Studies and Research (MCOENSSR). 
The MCOENSSR is envisioned as a Special Purpose Vehicle (SPV) to foster collaboration between academia, government, 
and industry in addressing national security challenges and developing a “Security Industrial Complex” under the vision of 
Atmanirbhar Bharat.
Leading institutions such as IIT Guwahati, IIT Delhi, IIT Kanpur, IIT Jodhpur, and IIT Dharwad, in partnership with the 
Indian tri-services, will drive innovation in defence technologies, with each institution specializing in specific domains. IIT 
Jodhpur will serve as the Centre of Excellence in Engine Design, UAVs, RPAs, Anti-Drone Systems, Stealth Technology, and 
Directed Energy Weapons, providing state-of-the-art infrastructure, domain expertise, and administrative support. The 
Institute will collaborate with partner institutions to identify critical research areas, facilitate resource sharing, and secure 
funding support from both government and private sectors.
The key focus areas of the MCOENSSR are:
I. Research and Development
II. Capacity Building
Multiple Entry-Exit systems
The Institute has introduced structured entry–exit policies for its BS, M.Tech., and Ph.D. programs, in line with the vision of 
the National Education Policy (NEP) 2020. Under these provisions, a BS student may exit with a B.Sc. degree in Physics or 
Chemistry. Similarly, M.Tech. and Ph.D. (Research) students may exit with a Diploma and M.S. by Research, respectively.

In addition, the Institute offers multiple entry schemes to facilitate academic mobility and lifelong learning. For 
undergraduate students, these schemes enable smooth progression into postgraduate programs. For M.Tech. students, the 
multiple entry option allows conversion to the M.Tech.–Ph.D. program after successful completion of two to three semesters. 
Such flexible pathways empower students to upskill and reskill at different stages of their professional careers. Furthermore, 
Direct Ph.D. students holding a B.Tech. degree have the option to pursue an additional M.Tech. degree by fulfilling the 
M.Tech. thesis requirements. This initiative is expected to enhance the Institute’s ability to attract high-quality students while
fostering a robust and sustainable research ecosystem.
The Institute proposes to introduce the following new academic programs from the Academic Year 2025–26:
•
B.Tech. in Electronics Engineering
•
M.Tech. in Drone and Anti-Drone Technologies
•
M.Tech. in Bridge Engineering
•
M.Des. in Smart Product Design
Implementation of Regional Language Teaching for First-Year UG Students
The Institute has introduced a provision for teaching in Hindi language for a section of first-year undergraduate students. To 
address language-related challenges, IIT Jodhpur has implemented a conversational instructional approach in first-year 
B.Tech. courses, with a focus on Hindi medium instruction. To maintain academic rigour and ensure uniform quality of
instruction, the same instructor teaches both the English and Hindi sections. This initiative, aligned with the vision of the
National Education Policy (NEP) 2020, seeks to enhance students’ comprehension of course material and encourage effective
classroom interaction. To support smooth transition into the B.Tech. program, the Institute has also established student
support services including language proficiency assessments, tutoring sessions, and language laboratories. This initiative not
only acknowledges the diverse linguistic backgrounds of students but also contributes to inclusive and equitable learning
outcomes.
A total of 116 students have opted for this provision in their first year of undergraduate study.
Direct Admission to Ph.D. program for Graduating B.Tech. Students of NITs
In pursuit of academic excellence, IIT Jodhpur has introduced a scheme for direct admission to Ph.D. programmes for 
meritorious B.Tech. students from various National Institutes of Technology (NITs), effective from the Academic Year 
2024–25. Under this provision, students who secure a CGPA of 8.0 or above and in top 10 rank in their class after the 7th 
semester are eligible for direct admission to the Ph.D. programme without the requirement of qualifying GATE or a written 
examination.
The selection process may be conducted through a brief online or in-person interview, or in certain cases, direct admission 
offers may be extended to eligible candidates.
Director’s Fellowship
In alignment with the Institute’s vision to promote the timely completion of academic programmes and to reward 
outstanding Ph.D. scholars, IIT Jodhpur has framed a policy for incentivizing time-efficient Ph.D. thesis submission.
Under this policy, the total emoluments (including MoE Fellowship) are structured as follows:
•
₹75,000 per month for scholars submitting their Ph.D. thesis within 3 years.
•
₹50,000 per month for scholars submitting their Ph.D. thesis after 3 years but within 4 years.
The detailed guidelines of this policy have been duly circulated among all stakeholders.
In addition to the above, the Institute has undertaken the following initiatives:
•
e-Senate: An e-Senate platform has been implemented to streamline processes prior to physical Senate meetings, thereby
enhancing the effectiveness and productivity of Senate deliberations.
•
Revised Academic Structure: In its 38th meeting held on 26 June 2024, the Senate approved a revised academic structure
with two tracks, namely, the Administrative Track and the Academic Track. The Academic Track comprises the
following Sub-Committees:
a.
Senate Undergraduate Committee (SUGC)
b.
Senate Postgraduate Committee (SPGC)
c.
Senate Online Education Committee (SOEC)

These Sub-Committees are aligned with the respective sections of the Office of Academic Affairs, with administrative 
operations overseen by the Dean of Academic Affairs (DoAA) in consultation with the Chairpersons of individual 
committees.
•
Blockchain-Based Digital Degrees: Marking a significant step towards transparency, authenticity, and student-centric
record management, IIT Jodhpur introduced blockchain-based secured digital degrees during its 10th Convocation. The
cryptographic hashing ensures that records remain immutable, while the adoption of Self-Sovereign Identity (SSI)
empowers students to control and share their tamper-proof digital credentials.
