RESEARCH & 
DEVELOPMENT

Introduction to the activities of the 
Office of R&D
Introduction to the activities of the Office of R&D
The Indian Institute of Technology Jodhpur places a strong emphasis on research, engaging in a wide range of activities 
including Sponsored Research projects, Consultancy assignments, Fellowships, Award Grants, and the organization of 
Conferences and Workshops. The Office of Research & Development plays a key role in supporting these efforts by 
offering dedicated administrative and managerial support for Sponsored Research, Consultancy work, and other related 
R&D initiatives. Furthermore, the R&D division of the Institute is consistently enhancing its research infrastructure by 
facilitating the development of state-of-the-art laboratories and aiding the utilization of cutting-edge technology for 
expanding research facilities.
Initiatives taken by the Office during the FY 2024-25
The Office of R&D has taken various steps to facilitate PIs and Inventors, which enables the smooth execution of projects.
Key initiatives are as follows:
•
Revision of R&D project manpower norms – abolition of loan policy and facility charge
•
Revision of Policy for Ad hoc appointment, Project Operation for DST Inspire / DST WOS, etc., and PDA share to
mentor, Guidelines for Student Top-up Fellowship to Ph. D Students, and Disbursement/Payment of honorarium
from projects.
•
Creation of the Institute Research and Development Committee(IRDC), consisting of faculty representatives from each
Department/School, dealing with policy creation and implementation.
•
Introduction of Faculty Research Excellence Award based on high-impact publication/technology development,
along with the existing three categories – Science, Engineering, and Management/Humanities.
•
CARE (Central Acquisition of Research Equipment) scheme has been introduced and implemented to facilitate
researchers in their ongoing research activities. One proposal towards research equipment is being supported in the
first round, amounting to Rs. 30 Lakhs under the scheme.
•
Several discussion meetings with ARDB, DIA-CoE, and the Indian Army have been conducted – initiation of research
collaboration with the Indian Defence sector.
•
Over the last one-year, the office has facilitated in significantly reaching the milestone of more than 100% growth in
project submission, project registration, and overhead generation.
•
Overhead amount of Rs. 3.57 Cr and project fund of Rs. 81.77 Cr are received in the financial Year 2024-25.
•
Facilitated the Establishment of Manekshaw Centre of Excellence for National Security Studies and Research
(MCOENSSR) for various research activities in defence technology during its initial phase.
International Mobility Research Grant (IMRG)
International Mobility Research Grant supported from R&D funds for providing an opportunity to young faculty 
members after following a rigorous two-stage peer review process for selection of projects. This scheme is for young 
faculty members to increase collaboration with internationally renowned researchers. Faculty members who have joined 
in the last three years and do not have international exposure are encouraged to visit and spend a two-month period 
during the summer vacation in international laboratories/industries. The first IMRG cycle is completed, and 8 FMs have 
been awarded Rs. 5 lakhs each for their international visit in March 2025.

MAJOR 
INSTITUTE EVENT

Major Institute Events
Awards & Recognition
IIT Jodhpur received the prestigious Grand Jury Winner Award in the Government Institute Category at the 
Confederation of Indian Industry – Industry Academia Partnership Awards 2024. This recognition, accepted by
Director Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal and Adviser to the Director Prof. Sampat Raj Vadera, underlines the Institute’s 
leadership in strengthening academia–industry collaboration and promoting innovation-driven education.
The Director’s pioneering research continues to bring global recognition to the Institute. Prof. Agarwal was listed in 
Stanford’s Top 2% Scientists worldwide for the fifth consecutive year and was also conferred the 3rd IETI Ramesh 
Agarwal Lifetime Achievement Award 2025 for his outstanding contributions to energy, combustion, and sustainable 
fuels.
Major Conferences & Summits
At the Rising Rajasthan Global Investment Summit 2024, IIT Jodhpur showcased its vision for contributing to 
Rajasthan’s sustainable growth. The Director emphasized the Institute’s preparedness for collaborations in renewable 
energy, healthcare, heritage conservation, and AI-based technologies. He also participated as a distinguished panelist in 
the Denmark Country Session on “Water Management for Liveable Cities”, where he presented IITJ’s initiatives for 
water security, climate resilience, and sustainable urban planning.
The Institute played a pivotal role at the 16th Prakriti International Documentary Film Festival, where the Director 
spoke on the importance of films as a medium to raise awareness about environmental protection and inspire sustainable 
practices.
The Institute also hosted an Awareness Workshop on the PoSH Act 2013, conducted by Supreme Court Advocate 
Ms. Aparna Bhat, which reinforced the Institute’s commitment to inclusivity and safe workplaces.
Media & Outreach
IIT Jodhpur enhanced its outreach through multiple media engagements. The Director appeared on DD National’s 
“Tech Trends: Technology for People” and DD Rajasthan’s “Vigyan Jagat”, sharing perspectives on science, 
sustainability, and technology for societal benefit. He also featured in a podcast on “EVs, AI & India’s Future Job 
Market”, addressing futuristic trends in employment. In addition, the Institute’s innovative initiatives were widely 
covered in leading national media, including The Hindu Business Line.
The Institute actively participated in the Visitor’s Conference 2024–25 at Rashtrapati Bhavan, inaugurated by the 
Hon’ble President of India, Smt. Droupadi Murmu. The event provided a platform for IIT Jodhpur to engage with 
national leadership and fellow higher education institutions.
New Centres & Programs
The Institute achieved a landmark milestone with the establishment of the Rishabh Centre for Research and Innovation 
in Clean Energy, supported by a generous ₹70 crore donation from Mr. Narendra Goliya, CMD, Rishabh Instruments
Limited. The Centre will drive cutting-edge clean energy research and foster innovation for a sustainable future.
IIT Jodhpur also launched the Integrated Teacher Education Programme (ITEP), a unique four-year BSc–BEd program 
with specializations in Physics, Chemistry, and Mathematics. Popularly known as the Jodhpur Model of Teacher Education, 
the program blends STEM education with design thinking and pedagogy, preparing high-quality school teachers for the 
future.
Further strengthening academic outreach, the Institute inaugurated the Centre for Continuing Education (CCE) to 
promote lifelong learning and professional development. To enhance the visibility of research, it also launched 
ScholarSphere: IITJ Research Insights Hub, a dedicated platform showcasing the scholarly contributions of its faculty.
Collaborations & Partnerships
The Institute forged several new collaborations during the year. MoUs were signed with Genpact for instituting a Chair 
Professorship and PhD fellowships, and with the Public Arts Trust of India to launch an Artist-in-Residence program. A 
partnership with the Jodhpur Pollution Control & Research Foundation focused on textile wastewater treatment, while 
collaboration with the All India Institute of Local Self-Government led to the creation of the Urban Resilience & 
Sustainability Hub.
Strengthening its academic ecosystem, IIT Jodhpur signed agreements with seven NITs (NITK Surathkal, NIT 
Jamshedpur, NIT Sikkim, MNIT Jaipur, NIT Meghalaya, NIT Hamirpur, and NIT Arunachal Pradesh), enabling direct 
PhD admissions for meritorious B.Tech graduates. On the global front, a European Union delegation visited IIT Jodhpur 
to explore Indo-European collaboration in research and innovation.

National Security & Defence Initiatives
IIT Jodhpur demonstrated its commitment to national priorities through key defense initiatives. The Manekshaw Centre 
of Excellence for National Security Studies and Research (MCOENSSR) was inaugurated, focusing on developing 
advanced technologies in UAVs, anti-drone systems, and directed energy weapons. The Institute also installed the 
Prithvi Missile System, marking a significant step in defense-related research infrastructure.
Further, IIT Jodhpur joined hands with IIT Guwahati, IIT Kanpur, IIIT Delhi, and CDAC to establish the National 
Security Innovation Hub, a consortium dedicated to driving indigenous defense technologies and supporting 
Atmanirbhar Bharat.
Faculty & Research Excellence
The Institute promoted international collaboration through the International Mobility Grant, awarding 5 lakhs each to 
eight faculty members across disciplines for joint projects with leading global universities. Additionally, in partnership 
with the American Chemical Society (ACS), the Institute hosted the program “Navigating PhD and Beyond”, which 
provided young researchers with training in scientific communication, sustainability, and professional growth.
Community Engagement
Beyond academic and research activities, the Institute remained actively engaged with the local community. The Director 
attended the Eye of Cyclone Felicitation Ceremony in Jodhpur, where 148 police officers and constables were honored 
for their exemplary service. This gesture highlighted IIT Jodhpur’s strong connection with regional institutions and 
communities.

FACILITIES

Digital Infrastructure & Automation (DIA)
The Digital Infrastructure & Automation (DIA), formerly known as the Computer Center, continues to serve as 
the digital backbone of IIT Jodhpur. As the pivotal hub for computing, networking, and automation, DIA plays 
an indispensable role in supporting research, academics, and administrative activities across the institute. Over 
the years, DIA has evolved in line with emerging technologies, reflecting IIT Jodhpur’s commitment to 
innovation, efficiency, and security. Today, it stands as a critical enabler of digital transformation within the 
campus.
Facilities & Infrastructure
High Performance Computing (HPC):
DIA operates one of the most advanced computing facilities in the region, offering over 450+ teraflops 
(FP64), 700+ teraflops (FP32) of computing power. With 3,500 CPU cores, 1 petabyte of storage delivering 20 
GBps throughput, and specialized infrastructure including 7 GPU nodes, 20 CPU nodes, and 2 AI 
supercomputers (DGX-A100), the HPC facility is a cornerstone for high-end computational research, particularly 
in AI/ML and interdisciplinary domains. Our HPC is listed in the C-DAC Top 100 HPC in India list.

Virtualization Cluster:
A robust virtualization setup with 8 high-end servers and 250 TB of storage supports more than 100 virtual machines. 
This infrastructure caters to both academic and administrative needs while ensuring optimized data center operations for 
improved efficiency and uptime.
Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP):
The Institute's ERP consolidates essential operations across Academics, Human Resources, Accounts, Research and 
Development, etc., and is equipped with a Decision Support System (DSS) to facilitate data-driven decision-making while 
reducing reliance on hardcopy documentation. The ERP system ensures safe authentication for all authorized 
stakeholders engaged in administrative and personal operations pertaining to the Institute.
CCLABs:
Currently DIA have two labs of total capacity 220 in Library building and currently upgradation of the computer lab 
facility of the institute is going on with doubling its capacity.
Networking & Connectivity:
The campus backbone now operates at 9 Gbps, powered by a 5 Gbps Airtel leased line, ensuring seamless connectivity 
across academic, research, and residential zones. With comprehensive LAN and Wi-Fi coverage, the institute also 
provides Eduroam, VPN, and secure guest access, supporting a connected academic ecosystem.
Cybersecurity:
Security remains a high priority. Following the completion of the VAPT audit, DIA has strengthened its defenses with 
advanced firewalls, endpoint protection, and mandatory HPC usage policies. Cyber threat intelligence is regularly shared 
with MeitY and CERT-In, ensuring proactive monitoring and response.
Software & Licensing:
A diverse portfolio of licensed software including MATLAB, Mathematica, Ansys, SolidWorks, Cadence, Synopsys, 
Mentor Graphics, and Ansoft supports academic and research activities. Open-source tools such as OwnCloud (private 
cloud) and Moodle (LMS) extend collaborative and learning capabilities across the campus.
Computer Labs:
DIA manages two well-equipped computer labs with a seating capacity of 220, located in the Library building. To meet 
growing demands, work is underway to double the lab capacity, further strengthening academic support.
Websites & Digital Platforms:
IIT Jodhpur’s website complies with GIGW standards, ensuring accessibility and usability. ERP modules continue to 
expand with functionality such as graduation processing, fiscal year closing, R&D proposal management, billing, and 
recruitment workflows.

Human Resources
To sustain and operate such a wide digital ecosystem, DIA is supported by a dedicated workforce. The team comprises 20 
regular staff, 4 project staff, and 8 outsourced staff, working collectively to maintain efficiency, reliability, and security 
across all services.
Major Initiatives during 2024–25
During the year, DIA undertook several significant initiatives aimed at enhancing IIT Jodhpur’s digital backbone, 
improving services, and ensuring robust security across platforms.
Network & ISP Upgradation:
To meet the growing demands of research and academic activities, DIA enhanced campus connectivity by securing a 5 Gbps 
leased line from Airtel. This expansion bolstered total bandwidth to 9 Gbps, enabling faster access to digital resources and 
ensuring uninterrupted network services across campus.
In October 2024, the entire campus backbone network including some servers was shifted from the Library Building to the 
Computer Center, ensuring that all data center services now operate under one roof.
Cybersecurity Enhancements:
DIA is working to strengthen the campus's cybersecurity posture by deploying open-source security solutions and sharing 
threat intelligence with CERT-In and MeitY. This initiative will help protect research and higher education institutions like 
ours, while contributing to the advancement of the national threat intelligence community.
IIT Jodhpur successfully onboarded to the Cyber Swachhta Kendra (CSK), enabling real-time monitoring of infected IPs and 
vulnerabilities. Furthermore, DIA organized cybersecurity awareness programs, beginning with first-year B.Tech students, 
to promote safe digital practices among users.
Digitization & Automation:
To advance paperless operations, DIA digitized all bills and invoices from the Accounts Section before the CAG audit. 
Additionally, 14,000+ large maps (A0, A1) from OIE and over 12.5 lakh archival office records were digitized. Academic 
Section records are now being digitized with department-wise access through a Document Management System (DMS) that 
provides searchable PDFs.
Deployment of e-Senate software was also completed, accompanied by faculty and staff training. A blockchain-based 
system for issuing and verifying academic credentials was also initiated, enhancing transparency and security.
ERP Development:
The ERP modules experienced substantial expansion throughout the year. Academic procedures, including graduation, 
convocation reporting, PhD supervision, and admissions (notably the new B.Sc.–B.Ed, BS/B.Sc programs), are now 
administered digitally. The Student Management System was implemented, accompanied by comprehensive digitalization 
of the Executive Education Program (EEP) degree, diploma, and certificate.
Finance modules, connectivity with Canara Bank, reconciliation with Paytm, budget oversight, vendor payment 
administration, and tax forecasting. An Annual Property Return system is being developed in Human Resources. 
System-level enhancements encompass SMS integration for two-factor authentication, alerting systems, and guest house 
administration.
ERP is now advancing towards Xapps (ERP for External Users), which facilitate functions such as Vendor Payment (Rent), 
Document Verification, Transcript Payment, Departmental Laboratory Services, and more.

Design Credit Project with Student:
Digital transformation is also providing younger students in the institute with opportunities to work on real-world projects. 
These projects not only benefit the institution but also help students achieve their learning objectives. The major outcomes 
of these collective efforts during this academic year such as
Implementation of Open Source Security Information and Event Management System with NIDS.
Student Visits:
As part of experiential learning and exposure activities, various groups of school and college students visited the 
state-of-the-art Data Centre at IIT Jodhpur. The visits aimed to provide young learners with first-hand insights into 
advanced digital infrastructure, high-performance computing systems, and the role of technology in research and 
innovation.
Strengths
•
Robust HPC infrastructure supporting interdisciplinary research.
•
Comprehensive ERP and digitization ecosystem, improving transparency and efficiency.
•
Campus-wide LAN and Wi-Fi coverage enabling seamless connectivity.
•
Proactive cybersecurity measures ensuring resilience and trust.
•
Well-defined IT usage policies and recommended practices that guide safe and responsible digital engagement.
Conclusion
DIA has firmly established itself as the cornerstone of IIT Jodhpur’s digital ecosystem, seamlessly integrating advanced 
computing resources, secure networks, and automation platforms. Its infrastructure not only supports cutting-edge 
research and academic excellence but also drives administrative efficiency and institutional transparency. Looking ahead, 
sustained investments in HPC, cybersecurity, and resilient networking will be vital for IIT Jodhpur to maintain its 
leadership in digital infrastructure and innovation.

S. R. Ranganathan Learning Hub: The Library
The S. R. Ranganathan Learning Hub, i.e., the library supports teaching and research activities of the Institute by 
facilitating acquisition, organization and dissemination of knowledge resources, and by providing library & information 
services to IIT Jodhpur community. It is situated prominently at the entrance of the academic area of the Institute, stands 
as the tallest structure on the campus scaling over 15m from the ground; keeps time for the entire campus with a 4-way 
clock at the clock tower, only the third in the city of Jodhpur. It functions under the guidance of the Library Committee, 
which has representatives from all Departments, and Student Representatives.
Collection: 
The Library has a rich and growing collection of approximately 19,000 volumes of books in print and electronic format, 
which include textbooks, and books of general and reference nature. A wide range of scholarly journals, databases and 
research support tools are subscribed from various sources for the academic and research purposes of the institute 
community.
Services & Facilities: The following services and facilities are provided by the library:
•
Member & Circulation Services
•
Orientation & User Education
•
Borrowing Facility
•
Reference & Information Service
Biometrics-enabled RFID technology
The library services are automated through biometrics enabled RFID technology using smart library solution for an 
effective management of the library and providing enhanced services like, self-check-out, self-check-in (book drop), 
security of materials, inventory management and finding misplaced items, stock verification, visitor counter, Smart Card 
issuance, etc.
Digital Resources: 
Library subscribes to a wide range of scholarly resources, like, journals, citation, indexing and scientometric databases, in 
all the thrust areas of academics and research of the Institute. In addition, the library subscribes and provides access to 
tools for academic and writing support, plagiarism detection, current and leisure reading, and off-campus resource access 
for the users. These resources are accessible through the user-friendly, responsive Library website, which is a 
comprehensive site maintained by Library. The website also provides online catalogue, lists of useful resources accessible 
in the open domain like the open access journals, books, repositories, video lectures, open courseware, and these are 
continuously updated.
The major journal resources include, American Chemical Society (ACS), American Institute of Physics (AIP), American 
Physical Society (APS), American Society for Civil Engineers (ASCE), American Society for Mechanical Engineers (ASME), 
Association for Computing Machinery (ACM), Elsevier Science Direct, Emerald Management Journals, IEEE Xplore 
Digital Library, Institute of Physics (IoP), Journal of Visualised Experiments (JoVE), JStor, Oxford University Press (OUP), 
Project MUSE, Royal Society of Chemistry (RSC), Sage Publishing, SciFinder Scholar, Scopus, Society for Industrial & 
Applied Mathematics (SIAM), Springer Nature, Taylor & Francis, and Web of Science.
Library Instruction Programs: 
Regular user orientation and library instruction sessions are organized for students by the Library Staff Members. Besides 
these, the library also organizes workshops and training sessions on using various resources, author workshops with 
experts, reference management, and library expert talks on trending topics in scholarly communication.

New Initiatives in FY 2024-25
The following new initiatives were taken by the library during the FY 2024-25:
•
The library has added to its collection a good number of books and subscription to 48 major scholarly resources,
including academic journals, research databases, and digital tools designed to assist students and researchers in their
work.
•

library was able to facilitate full-text access to journal resources from around 30 world-renowned publishers through
central funding.
•
A significant milestone was the development of “ScholarSphere: IITJ Research Insights Hub”, a dedicated platform
designed to preserve and provide seamless access to the scholarly contributions of its faculty. From journal papers and
conference proceedings to books and technical reports, ScholarSphere serves as a centralized repository aimed at
enhancing research visibility, accessibility, and collaboration. This platform, which is developed using DSpace Current
Research Information System (CRIS) flavour and integrated with ORCiD login, was launched on the occasion of
National Science Day on 28th February 2025 by Sh. Sharad Kumar Saraf, Chairman-BoG, IIT Bombay, and Chairman
& Managing Director, Technocraft Industries (India) Limited, Mumbai. This initiative underscores IIT Jodhpur’s
commitment to nurturing a robust research ecosystem that inspires innovation and global academic engagement.
•
Besides contributing to scholarly publications, this year, the library staff members regularly participated in
professional development programs and activities, delivering talks and presentations. A noteworthy achievement this
year is that Mr. Tapas Kumar Das, Assistant Librarian, and Mr. Kamlesh Patel, Assistant Library Information Officer,
have been awarded the Ph.D. degree in Library and Information Science.

Inclusivity Cell
Preamble
We, the fraternity of IIT Jodhpur, join together in a spirit of respect, understanding, and commitment to fostering an 
environment where every individual feels valued, supported, and empowered.
We recognize all people's inherent dignity and worth, regardless of their race, ethnicity, nationality, gender identity, sexual 
orientation, age, ability, religion, or any other aspect of their identity.
As stewards of inclusivity, we strive to create a space that celebrates diversity and champions equity. We acknowledge the 
importance of actively listening to diverse voices, engaging in meaningful dialogue, and advocating for justice and 
equality for all.
In our pursuit of inclusivity, we commit to challenging bias, discrimination, and exclusion wherever they may arise. We 
embrace the richness of perspectives that diversity brings and seek to learn from each other's unique experiences and 
backgrounds.
Through our collective efforts, we aspire to create a culture of belonging where everyone feels welcome, respected, and 
empowered to thrive. Together, we stand as allies and advocates, united in our dedication to building a more inclusive and 
equitable community.
With this preamble as our guide, we embark on a journey of continuous learning, growth, and action towards a more just 
and inclusive society for all.
Introduction
INCLUSION is intricately linked to diversity, equity, accessibility, and belonging. A diverse, equitable, inclusive, and 
accessible culture:
•
Seeks to create a culture with a mix of people from different backgrounds of all types (races, sexes, religions, national
origins, physical disabilities, sexual orientation and gender expression, size, and age).
•
Commits to fair treatment, access, opportunity, and advancement for all people.
•
Values every person and their unique approach to the work.
•
Optimizes for all people, including people with disabilities, to fully and independently collaborate and work
successfully.
An inclusive culture helps all members of a workplace contribute to a sense of belonging and community, promotes a 
healthier and more empowering work environment and teams, respects differences, and optimizes for equal opportunities. 
This type of culture also shares power within teams—and with the public, whose work ultimately benefits.
Equality
Equality is the state of being equal, especially in status, rights, and opportunities. Equality means each individual or group 
of people is given the same resources and opportunities, regardless of their circumstances.
Promoting equality and valuing diversity is fundamental to the Institute’s core values and mission, with the principles of 
inclusiveness, tolerance, and fairness central to our legitimacy as an Institute. The Institute does not accept unfair 
discrimination or less favorable treatment as an employer or in the running of the Institute on the grounds of age, 
disability, gender reassignment, marriage/civil partnership, pregnancy/maternity/paternity, race, religion, belief, refugee 
and asylum seekers (as per the Government of India norms), sex, or sexual orientation.
Ethical Policy
Having an ethical Institutional policy that provides guidance for employees and other internal stakeholders on ethical 
behaviors can reduce misbehavior in the Institute.
Additionally, a strong ethical culture can help to create a culture of accountability, as employees are more likely to be held 
responsible for their actions when ethics is an integral part of the institutional culture, increased employee job satisfaction, 
affective commitment, and willingness to recommend their institution to others.
Implementation of the Government of India Reservation policies / Welfare measures
One of the main objectives of the Inclusivity Cell is to implement the Government of India Reservation Policies / Welfare 
measures for Scheduled Castes (SC) / Scheduled Tribes (ST) / Other Backward Class (OBC)/ Persons with Disability 
(PWD) / Economically Weaker Section (EWS) / LGBTQ & other Minority Communities about the Admission of Students, 
the Recruitment of Faculty and Non-faculty positions, and other benefits, as applicable.

Scheduled Castes (SC)
Scheduled Castes are those castes/races in the country that are notified as Scheduled Castes as per provisions contained in 
Clause 1 of Article 341 of the Constitution. 
More details are available on the below link:
https://documents.doptcirculars.nic.in/D2/D02adm/Introductory.pdf
The Constitution of India has prescribed protection and safeguards for the Scheduled Castes (SCs), Scheduled Tribes (STs), 
and other weaker sections, either specially or the way of insisting on their general rights as citizens, with the object of 
promoting their educational and economic interests and removing social disabilities. These social groups have also been 
provided institutionalized commitments through the statutory body, the National Commission of SCs. The Ministry of 
Social Justice & Empowerment is the nodal Ministry that oversees the interests of the Scheduled Castes.
Scheduled Tribes (ST)
The term 'Scheduled Tribes' first appeared in the Constitution of India. Article 366
(25) defined scheduled tribes as "such tribes or tribal communities or parts of or groups within such tribes or tribal
communities as are deemed under Article 342 to be Scheduled Tribes for the purposes of this constitution". Article 342,
reproduced below, prescribes the procedures to be followed in the specification of scheduled tribes.
https://documents.doptcirculars.nic.in/D2/D02adm/Introductory.pdf
Other Backward Class (OBC)
The Other Backward Class (OBC) is a collective term used by the Government of India to classify educationally or socially 
backward castes. It is one of several official classifications of the population of India, along with General castes, Scheduled 
Castes, and Scheduled Tribes (SCs and STs).
Criteria to identify the portion of the population comprising the “creamy layer” have been recommended, including the 
following:
Children of those with a family income above Rs.8,00,000/- a year should be considered creamy layer and excluded from 
the reservation quota. 
The OBC list presented by the National Commission for Backward Classes is dynamic (castes and communities can be 
added or removed) and is subject to change from time to time depending on social, educational, and economic factors. For 
example, the OBCs are entitled to 27 % reservations in Public Sector Employment and Higher Education. In the 
Constitution, OBCs are described as ‘socially and educationally backward classes,’ and the government is enjoined to 
ensure their social and educational development.
Persons with Disability (PWD) (Divyang; दिव्यांगजन)
The Government of India has enacted the Rights of Persons with Disabilities Act, 2016, which gives effect to the United 
Nations Convention on the Rights of Persons with Disabilities and for matters connected therewith or incidental thereto. 
WHEREAS the United Nations General Assembly adopted its Convention on the
Rights of Persons with Disabilities on the 13th day of December 2006. AND WHEREAS the aforesaid Convention lays 
down the following principles for the empowerment of persons with disabilities:
a.
respect for inherent dignity, individual autonomy, including the freedom to make one's own choices, and
independence of persons;
b.
non-discrimination;
c.
full and effective participation and inclusion in society;
d.
respect for difference and acceptance of persons with disabilities as part of human diversity and humanity;
e.
equality of opportunity;
f.
accessibility;
g.
equality between men and women;
h.
respect for the evolving capacities of children with disabilities and respect for the right of children with disabilities to
preserve their identities.
Empowerment of Persons with Disabilities (PwD)
Initiatives are taken by IIT Jodhpur towards empowerment of Persons with Disabilities (PwD) to facilitate their 
participation in all walks of life and enjoy their rights equally with dignity and respect:

•
Medical clinic with well-equipped facilities 24*7 and night duty doctors/attendants. Ambulance service is also
provided 24*7 for all students.
•
IIT Jodhpur is encouraging the PwD students to participate actively in culture and sports activities and has initiated
coaching camps in various sports and games.
•
The Institute provides hostel accommodations to students with disabilities on the ground floors for easy access to
services and resources in different hostels located at the IIT campus.
•
Ramps, lifts, and separate washrooms are available in all the buildings of the Institute for the convenience of students
with disability.
•
The Student Wellbeing Committee is especially sensitive to the needs of students with disability and provides the
required psychological support.
•
Providing transport facilities for differently abled students.
•
Scholarship for Students with Disabilities as per GOI Guidelines.
•
The Institute is following the guidelines of the ‘Rights of Persons with Disabilities (RPWD) Act, 2016, for the candidates
belonging to the PwD category, like providing Scribe /compensatory time for examination and easy access to
classrooms through ramps/lifts, etc.
•
The Institute has ramps and lifts for students and employees with disabilities in all academic buildings, residential
buildings, and student hostels.
•
Also, accessible toilets for disabled persons are available in all the hostels and academic buildings. Residential
buildings are constructed based on the requirements.
Some photos of the facilities that are provided by IITJ to the PwD employees and Students:
Ramps
Lifts
Washroom

•
Screen Reader for Visually Impaired Users: The Screen Reader facility in the library of IIT Jodhpur is a significant step
towards ensuring equal access to information for visually impaired users. This technology converts text on the
computer screen into speech or Braille, allowing visually impaired users to navigate and use the library's resources
more independently. The introduction of screen readers not only supports visually impaired users in their academic
pursuits but also promotes their overall inclusion in the academic community. By providing this facility, the library
demonstrates its commitment to creating an inclusive and accessible environment for all users, regardless of their
physical abilities. This initiative aligns with the broader trend of incorporating assistive technologies in libraries to
enhance accessibility for individuals with disabilities. By adopting these technologies, libraries can significantly
improve the learning experience for visually impaired users and contribute to their academic success.
Economically Weaker Section (EWS)
Persons who are not covered under the scheme of reservation for SCs, STs, and OBCs and whose family has a gross annual 
income below Rs. 8 Lakh (Rupees eight lakh only) are to be identified as EWSs for the benefit of reservation. Income shall 
also include income from all sources, i.e., salary, agriculture, business, profession, etc., for the financial year prior to the 
year of application.
1.
Also, persons whose family owns or possesses any of the following assets shall be excluded from being identified as
EWS, irrespective of the family income:
A. 5 acres of agricultural land and above;
B.
Residential area of 1000 sq. ft. and above;
C.
Residential plot of 100 sq. yards and above in notified municipalities;
D. Residential plots of 200 sq. yards and above in areas other than the notified municipalities.
2.
The property held by a "Family" in different locations or different places/cities would be clubbed while applying for
the land or property holding test to determine EWS status.
3.
The term "Family" for this purpose will include the person who seeks the benefit of reservation, his/her parents, and
siblings below the age of 18 years, as well as his/her spouse and children below the age of 18 years.
LGBTQ
LGBTQ is an umbrella term used to refer to lesbian, gay, bisexual, transgender, and queer. LGBTQ people represent a 
subset of individuals among the broader category of sexually and gender-diverse individuals. Sexual orientation, gender 
identity, and expression (SOGIE) is diverse and spans cultures across the world.
The Inclusivity Cell is entrusted to protect the rights of the LGBTQ community.
International Community
The IIT Jodhpur has a vibrant cohort of International Students. IIT Jodhpur warmly welcomes the international community 
from across the globe. The existing Office of International Relations promotes and assists candidates in pursuing their 
dreams through education in the Institute's various UG and PG programs. The Institute provides opportunities for holistic 
growth of the International Community without any discrimination. Presently, the Institute is admitting foreign nationals 
through the following schemes with opportunities for Scholarships:

•
Study in India (SII) Scheme
•
Indian Council for Cultural Relations Scholarships (ICCR)
•
The Association of South East Asian Nations (ASEAN)
In line with the Government of India Policy, the Inclusivity Cell at IIT Jodhpur has been entrusted with the proper 
implementation and adoption of reservation policies and guidelines issued by the Government of India from time to time. 
The Cell deals with grievances from employees and students of SC, ST, OBC, PwD, EWS, and LGBTQ 
Category/community of the Institute. The Cell is also responsible for preparing/verifying the report(s) and addressing 
queries raised by the Ministry of Education, Govt. of India, related to the students and employees of the above categories 
of the Institute.
The inclusivity Cell at IIT Jodhpur is committed to implementing the above- mentioned policies of the Ministry of 
Education and the Govt. of India effectively to achieve comprehensive inclusion and diversity.
IIT Jodhpur follows the reservation norms of Govt. of India for candidates under the SC, ST, OBC, PwD, and EWS 
categories for admission in all UG and PG programs. The Institute provides the relaxation in eligibility criteria and 
application fees to SC, ST, and PwD candidates at the time of admission. The PwD students are exempted from paying the 
Tuition Fee. IIT Jodhpur participates in preparatory courses for one year for SC, ST, and PwD candidates who applied for 
undergraduate courses in IITs. On successful completion of the course, the students are offered direct admission to the 
already allocated undergraduate course the next year.
Further, to help students with academic deficiencies, especially SC, ST, and PwD Students, the following support 
mechanisms are created:
•
There is a provision for academic probation for students with academic deficiency. A student placed on probation shall
be monitored, including mandatory attendance in classes, special tutorials, and mentoring. Mentoring would comprise
structured guidance under a senior student.
•
These students can get B.Tech./B.Sc. in Engineering Science after completing the credit requirements as an exit degree
for those with academic deficiency.
•
Relaxation in minimum requirement on credits earned for continuation in a B.Tech. Program.
•
Relaxation in CGPA for branch change
•
Language support: Language is an important axis for inclusion/exclusion. The Institute is committed to providing
language training to students who need it. For non-Hindi speakers (Indian and foreign) on campus, providing Hindi
language support.
Fee remission is applicable for UG students as per the Ministry of Education, Govt. of India guidelines as given below:
•
SC, ST & PwD are eligible to get a full Tuition fee waiver.
•
Economically Weaker Section (EWS) Students (whose family income is less than Rs. 1 lakh per annum) are eligible for
full fee remission.
•
The other economically backward students (whose family income is between Rs. 1 lakh to Rs. 5 lakhs per annum) shall
get remission of 2/3rd of the fee.
•

Anti-Discrimination Policy
The Anti-Discrimination Policy emphasizes creating a safe and inclusive workplace by preventing discrimination based on 
protected characteristics. It details the behaviors considered discriminatory and the actions taken against such behaviors, 
promotes fairness, equality, and positive work culture, and ensures all stakeholders of the Institute are treated with respect 
and dignity, regardless of their background or identity.
Employees who harass their colleagues will go through the Institute's disciplinary process, and the Institute may 
reprimand, demote, or terminate them depending on the severity of their offense.
Anti-Harassment Policy
The Anti-harassment policy emphasizes a commitment to a harassment-free environment. It prohibits intimidation, 
humiliation, sabotage, and discrimination based on various factors.

The anti-harassment policy expresses the Institute’s commitment to maintaining a workplace that’s free of harassment so 
the employees can feel safe and happy. The Institute does not tolerate anyone intimidating, humiliating, or sabotaging 
others in the workplace. The Institute also prohibits willful discrimination based on age, sexual orientation, ethnicity, race, 
religion, or disability.
This anti-harassment policy, including sexual harassment, applies to all Institute stakeholders. Harassment includes 
bullying, intimidation, direct insults, malicious gossip, and victimization.
The consequences for violating the policy can vary based on the severity and frequency of the offense. They can range from 
counseling sessions to educate the offender about their behavior, written reprimands added to their personnel file, 
suspensions without pay, or even termination in severe cases.
Internal Complaints Committee (ICC)
The Institute has formulated IIT Jodhpur (Prevention, Prohibition and Redressal of Sexual Harassment) Rules, 2023 in line 
with Sexual Harassment of Women at Workplace (Prevention, Prohibition and Redressal) Act, 2013, Government of India 
to deal with Sexual Harassment. The mandate of the Internal Complaints Committee (ICC) is to evolve a mechanism for 
the prevention and redressal of any type of Sexual harassment complaints.
https://iitj.ac.in/footer/index.php?id=anti_sexual_harassment_policy
Grievance Redressal Mechanism
IIT Jodhpur has a robust Grievances Redressal mechanism to address all types of grievances, complaints, and malpractices, 
including those received from Students, Faculty, and other Stakeholders of the Institute.
Having a good grievance structure in place has multiple benefits, but the chief advantage is that it ensures that the Institute 
maintains positive employee relations. Effective grievance procedures promote consistency, transparency, and fairness in 
dealing with workplace complaints.
Disciplinary Committee
The Disciplinary Committee ensures compliance with the Code of Discipline and Conduct for students and will suggest 
suitable action in case of its violation. In case of matters concerning the Institute, the Disciplinary Committee is empowered 
to make decisions.
A student shall invite disciplinary action from the Institute if he/she violates the Code of Conduct; the actions may include 
reprimand, disciplinary probation, fine, debarring from examinations, withdrawal of scholarship and/or placement 
services, withholding of grades and/or degrees, cancellation of registration, and even expulsion from the Institute.
https://iitj.ac.in/assets/uploads/document/2024/04/2024-04-15-661d4bc916500- 1713195977.pdf

Primary Health Center IIT Jodhpur
The Health Centre (HC) has been started at the Permanent Campus of IIT Jodhpur from 15 June 2017. IIT Jodhpur provides 
round-the-clock health care facilities to Students, Faculty/ Staff Members and their dependents, also other residents and 
working staff of the Institute.
This fully equipped and self-sufficient facility is run under the supervision of Professor-in-charge Health Center (PIC HC) 
and Medical Officers (MO) with advice provided by the Medical Service User’s Committee (MSUC).
Presently, the following facilities are available at the Primary Health Centre (PHC):
1.
Medical Officers (24 x 7),
2.
Regular visits of specialist doctors (Psychiatrist, Gynaecologist, Paediatrician, ENT, Medicine, Orthopaedician),
3.
Nursing Officers, male & female (24 x7),
4.
Diagnostic laboratory,
5.
Physiotherapy unit,
6.
In-house Pharmacy,
7.
24 x7 Emergency Room and Daycare Room,
8.
Separate male and female wards and Isolation Rooms,
9.
01 ACLS (Advanced Cardiac Life Support) Ambulance,
10. Ayurvedic, Homeopathic and Naturopathic and other consultants visit twice a week.
Hospital Tie-Ups and Medical Support Network
In addition to on-campus healthcare, IIT Jodhpur has established formal agreements with several leading hospitals to 
ensure priority treatment for its students, faculty, staff, and their registered dependents.
These include (1) Goyal Hospital and Research Centre, (2) MediPulse Hospital, (3) ASG Eye Hospital, and (4) 
Vasundhara Hospital. 
Stakeholders may also avail of medical services at AIIMS Jodhpur, S.N. Medical College, and other State Government 
Hospitals as needed.
The Institute Health Center (PHC) plays a central role in coordinating and supervising the treatment of patients admitted 
to these empanelled hospitals. This ensures continuity of care and assistance during hospitalization.
Extension of Medical Services
•
Visitors to the Institute may access basic healthcare services through the Health Center during their stay on campus,
upon request.
•
In emergency situations, medical services are extended to non-IIT Jodhpur community members residing in the
campus area to provide timely first aid and support.
Arrangements are routinely made for specialist doctor visits on the campus (Psychiatrist, Gynaecologist, Paediatrician, 
ENT Specialists, Endocrinologist, Orthopedic Specialist) on a weekly basis. 
The Health Center also organizes various Health Awareness, Medical Screening, Vaccination Camps and Blood donation 
camps in coordination with Hospitals and other Agencies.
The Health Center is the first point of contact for any medical needs, and it aims to cater & provide primary health care to 
the students, staff, faculties, and their dependent(s) in the campus.
Arrangements are routinely made for specialist doctor visits on the campus (Psychiatrist, Gynaecologist, Paediatrician, 
ENT Specialists, Endocrinologist, Orthopedic Specialist) on a weekly basis.

4. Health Center Services
The Health Center offers a wide range of services, including:
4.1 Emergency Services
•
A 24×7 Emergency/Casualty Room is available for immediate medical attention.
•
Equipped with emergency medicines, ECG machine, defibrillator, and cardiac monitors.
•
Minor OT procedures and daycare admissions are facilitated.
•
If further management is required, the patient is referred to empanelled tertiary hospitals by the attending Medical
Officers.
4.2 Pharmacy
•
The on-campus AMRIT Pharmacy operates round-the-clock, dispensing prescribed medicines.
•
Medicines not available immediately are procured and provided at the earliest under 48 hours.
4.3 Laboratory Services
•
Laboratory is operational daily for routine investigations.
•
Laboratory services are available from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, supported by one of the empanelled Hospitals.
4.4 Referral Services
Patients requiring advanced or specialized treatment are referred to empanelled hospitals:
•
Goyal Hospital
•
Medipulse Hospital
•
Vasundhara Hospital
•
ASG Eye Hospital (Pal Link Road, and Paota)
•
Institute employees receive cashless treatment; students receive treatment at subsidized CGHS rates after referral by
Medical Officers.

•

▪
Blood donation drives
▪
Thematic health clinics, e.g., Adolescent Health Clinic, Lifestyle Disease Management Clinic

hygiene and food quality in hostel mess facilities.

a week.

Services include Ayurveda, Homeopathy, and Naturopathy consultations for holistic wellness.

Sundays).

STUDENT AFFAIR

Registered Students A.Y. 2024-25
Student Life at IIT Jodhpur
1. Institute Welcome and Orientation Program 2024
The Institute Welcome and Orientation program was organized by the Office of Students in the months of July and 
August for the newly enrolled UG and PG students for the academic year 2024-25. Various events were planned in 
the orientation program like Shubhaarambh, Fiesta 2024, PG excursion, etc. The purpose of the programme was to 
help students with the transition to the new chapter in their lives by welcoming them as a part of the IITJ 
community and making them feel at home. This seeks to help the faculty and administration at IITJ understand 
student aspirations and family expectations and then communicate their commitment to making the student 
experience worthwhile and pleasant. Refreshments were provided to all the participants during the program.
2. Janmashtami Celebrations 2024
On the occasion of Janmashtami, the Dahi Handi and Tug of War competitions were organized Hostel-wise by the 
Board of Student Welfare on the ground in front of the I2 Hostel on 26th August 2024. The students showcased their 
strength, teamwork, and competitive spirit by enthusiastically participating in the Dahi Handi and Tug of War 
Competition. All the IITJ Fraternity came together to celebrate this occasion and shared the joy and unity with full 
devotion.
3. National Sports Day 2024
On the occasion of the birthday of the Hockey legend Major Dhyan Chand and to commemorate India’s deep 
rooted tradition of sports, National Sports Day, 2024 was celebrated on 29th August 2024 from 6:00 PM onwards, 
under which various activities like 5 km Rally, Fit INDIA Pledge, Prize distribution of Fresher’s sports tournament, 
Exhibition match of students (Kabaddi, Football) were scheduled by the Office of Students for all Students, Faculty 
members, Staff and their family members at the Milkha Singh Sports Complex, IITJ campus.
4. Ganeshotsava 2024:
Ganeshotsav, a vibrant and culturally rich festival, was celebrated in IIT Jodhpur from 7th September to 13th 
September. This joyous occasion featured a range of traditional events, including sustainable and eco-friendly 
Ganesh idol making, rangoli competitions, Kabaddi, and other cultural events, all aimed at promoting and 
preserving our heritage. All the students & staff together as a community welcomed Lord Ganesha at the IITJ 
main gate and then carried on with the procession till B-5 ground mandap. Each day began and ended with an 
aarti puja, fostering a sense of community and spiritual connection amongst the student fraternity. The festival 
promises to be a blend of devotion, creativity, and cultural pride, making it a memorable experience for all campus 
residents.

5. World Suicide Prevention Day 2024:
On the occasion of World Suicide Prevention Day, an awareness signature campaign was organized for all the staff members. 
The event started at 10:30 a.m. at the admin building (Chanakya Complex East Wing). The staff members joined the campaign 
and took pledge to prevent the suicide prevention by signing on the standee at the venue.
6. Sandstone Summit 4.0:
The flagship event of IIT Jodhpur "Sandstone Summit 4.0" was organized on 28th & 29th September, 2024 at I2 Informal 
Grounds. This event aimed to initiate a collaborative engagement between industry leaders and students through a series of 
diverse and creative event concepts designed to encourage a broad discourse, such as panel discussions, standalone sessions, 
and technical activities. This year, the sandstone summit 4.0 was hosted for the first time on the beautiful 852 acres of the vast 
IIT Jodhpur campus with a theme “Automating Tomorrow: Sustainable Strategies in Intelligent Tech”. This event allowed 
students for real-time exchange of ideas between Industry and Academia. The 4th edition of Sandstone Summit 4.0 delved 
into the future of technology-driven sustainability with discussions centered around the following sub-themes:
•
Green Automation for a Sustainable Future: Integrating intelligent automation to foster eco-friendly industries.
•
Ethical AI and Tech for Tomorrow: Balancing innovation with responsibility to ensure long-term societal benefits.
•
Resilient Systems in an Automated World: Building robust, adaptable systems to navigate the complexities of a rapidly
changing environment.
•
Collaborative Innovation: Bridging academia and industry for sustainable technological advancements.
Various events were planned in this summit like Leadership Talks Featuring VPs, MDs, and CEOs of leading firms and 
startups from across the nation and the globe; Panel Discussions with prominent industry experts, including hiring managers, 
technical managers, and product managers from top MNCs; and other activities such as Hackathons, Ideathons, and Case 
Studies curated with companies to help you land your dream internship or placement opportunity.
7. Navratri/Garba Celebration 2024:
Navratri is a festival celebrating the goddess Durga over nine nights, symbolizing the victory of good over evil. The Office of 
Students organized the Navratri 2024 festivities for nine days from 02nd to 10th October 2024 in the Director’s Lawn at IIT 
Jodhpur from 7:00 PM onwards. The events planned under the celebrations were: Ram Leela, Traditional Garba and Dandiya 
Dance Performances with traditional navratri music; Religious ceremony including the Mataji ki Aarti. Food stalls and 
Dandiya stalls were also set up at the above-mentioned venue during the entire Navratri celebration. All students, Staff and 
Faculty members enthusiastically participated in the celebration.
8. TEDx 2024:
TEDx is a platform to connect with like-minded peers and professionals. This year TEDx was scheduled on October 5, 2024. 
The event was inaugurated by our Honourable Director, Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal. The event was graced by various 
dignitaries like Shri Suhas Yathiraj, Dr. Gunjan Malhotra, Ms. Nithya Rajendran, Col. Shivendra Pratap Singh Kanwar, Shri 
Nalin Shinghal, Shri Aashish Sharma, Shri Sujeet Singh, Shri Gaurav Sen and Ms. Devyani Shorey. This one-day event 
fostered collaborations, inspired students to think differently and pursue their passions, and offered an exceptional 
opportunity to engage with dynamic personalities and our esteemed speakers from various domains like Entrepreneurship, 
Indian Army officials, Bureaucrats, Entertainment, Corporate and Social Workers, etc. opening doors to various 
opportunities and ideas.
9. Varchas 2024
The annual inter-college Sports Festival of IIT Jodhpur and the largest sporting event in North-West India, Varchas 24 was 
organized by the Office of Students from 10th to 12th October 2024 in the Sports Complex. The opening ceremony involved 
the Olympics inspired Torch Bearing Ceremony by distinguished sports individuals of our Institute, followed by the Oath 
Taking ceremony which also took place on 09th October 2024 from 6.00 PM onwards in the Football Ground near Akash 
Building. The event featured a series of cultural performances of Malkham and rhythmic Yoga, Motivational speeches, Sports 
events and ceremonial moments embodying the spirit of sportsmanship. Along with the sports events, a Star Night with the 
Band “Lost Stories" and “DJ AZTEC” were also organized on 12th October 2024 at I2 Hostel Grounds. The closing ceremony 
for the same was held on 12th October at 5.00 PM in LHC 110.

11. 10th Convocation 2024:

was presided over by Shri A. S. Kiran Kumar, Chairman BOG, IIT Jodhpur while Prof. Avinash Kumar Agarwal, Director, IIT 
Jodhpur delivered the welcome address and presented the Institute Report. The event witnessed the inauguration of AIOT

campus infrastructure and fostering a vibrant community for the Institute’s academic staff. This year the convocation 
ceremony was organized into two sessions: In the forenoon session, degrees were awarded to the 1085 graduates of the 
Institute followed by oath taking by the graduates. For the first time in the history of IIT Jodhpur, the mark of 1000 students 
graduating in a year has been crossed. In the afternoon session, the Office of Students presented Awards and Certificates of 
Merit to the top performers in the field of Non-Academic Achievement. Out of 29 Award winners, 05 were the gold medalists, 
22 were silver medalists and 02 students got the bronze medals in the Non-Academic Achievement field. This year the 
provision for Bronze medals was introduced for the first time for the passed out students. The event concluded with the 
National Anthem followed by the Alumni Induction dinner for the students and their parents.
12. Inter IIT Sports Meet 2024:
Inter-IIT Sports Meet is the annual sports tournament of all the Indian Institute of Technology and the longest-running 
inter-collegiate meet where all IITs participate, having been held since 1961. This year, the 57th Inter-IIT Sports Meet 2024 was 
jointly organized by IIT Indore and IIT Kanpur from 10th December to 17th December 2024. A total of 167 members 
(contingents and staff members) participated in both the IITs. The Inter IIT Sports Meet brought together athletes from 
various IITs across the country to compete in a wide range of sporting events. Our teams showcased exceptional talent and 
dedication, competing fiercely against formidable opponents. Despite the tough competition, our athletes secured impressive 
results, including the Gold Medal in Table Tennis-(Women), Bronze medal in Badminton-(Men), Silver Medal in Chess, and 
Bronze medal in Squash (Men) in the Inter IIT Sports Meet underscored our competitive spirit and determination to excel on 
the national stage.

13. Inter IIT Tech Meet 2024:
Inter-IIT Tech Meet is the annual technical competition of all the Indian Institute of Technology which provides a 
unique platform to engage with the core technical fields in various IITs, foster teamwork, and showcase the talent. 
This year, the 13th edition of the Inter IIT Tech Meet was organized by IIT Bombay from 11th to 14th December 
2024. A total of 72 students participated at IIT Bombay. This year, a historic milestone has been achieved by IIT 
Jodhpur at the Inter IIT Tech Meet 13.0! Our students have secured 3rd position in ISRO HIGH PREP PROBLEM 
STATEMENT INTER IIT and 2nd position in Tag Team. From a lacklustre 21st rank just a couple of years ago, 
IIT Jodhpur has soared into the Top 10, amassing an impressive 1201 points marking a phenomenal transformation in 
the tech culture of the institute. This journey underscores the resilience, dedication, and relentless efforts of our tech 
community, establishing IIT Jodhpur as a rising force in the tech ecosystem.
14. Inter IIT Cult Meet 2024:
Inter-IIT Cult Meet is the annual cultural competition of all the Indian Institute of Technology which provides a 
unique platform to engage with the diverse cultural heritage of various IITs, foster teamwork, and showcase the talent. 
This year, the 7th edition of the Inter IIT Cultural Meet was organized by IIT Patna from 26th to 29th December 2024. A 
total of 148 students participated in 12 Cultural Cups at IIT Patna. The See-Off Ceremony for the participants of the Inter 
IIT Cultural Meet 7.0 took place at LHC 110 on 22nd December 2024 from 6PM to 8PM before departing for the 
host IIT Patna. The talented participants showcased captivating performances with dedication and creativity. With 
each edition, the students learn valuable lessons and enhance their performances across the multiple events. Our 
students won a Bronze medal in the Cook off competition. 
15. PROMETEO 2025:
Prometeo’25, the 5th edition of IIT Jodhpur’s annual technical and Entrepreneurial festival was organized by the 
Board of Innovation & Entrepreneurship (BIE) from 17th to 19th January 2025 at the Lecture Hall Complex Building and 
the Informal Grounds of the campus. This fest featured a dynamic blend of talks, workshops, exhibitions, 
and technical and various entrepreneurial competitions like Robowar, RC XP Zone, Drone Zone, etc. Through live 
demos, hackathons, and workshops, participants showcase their technical expertise and innovative thinking. 
The theme for this year was "Nordic Nights: Illuminating Vedic Visions" drawing a compelling parallel 
between the rich cultural tapestries of the Nordic and Vedic traditions, highlighting their shared themes of 
resilience, exploration, and the pursuit of knowledge. The main events of the said An Exhibition by Border Security 
Force (BSF), Quantum Cube’s Experience Zone, and RC Plane Show by the Indian Air Force were the main events of 
Prometeo 2025. The technical fest ended with the performance by the Sangam band and D.J. Aashish.

Ignus is a vibrant platform that inspires personal and creative growth through interactive workshops, 
captivating performances, 
and

Jodhpur from 06th to 09th of February, 2025. The theme for Ignus 2025 was “Melting Mosaic: Sanskriti ka 
Sangam”. The event was inaugurated at the Lecture Hall Complex on 6th February 2025. The major flagship 
events of Ignus 2025 were: Nityansh - Group Dance, Antarang - The Fashion Show, Aayaam-Nukkad Natak, 
and Thunder Beats-Clash of Bands. IGNUS 2025 witnessed a mesmerizing and enthralling performance by 
DJ Ravator on 8th February 2025 and a mesmerizing and enthralling performance by the renowned Music 
Composer and Singer Amaal Malik and team on 9th February 2025. 
17. Social Excursion / Visit 2024- Non Graded Courses:
The Institute offers Non-Graded Courses for B. Tech, B.S. and B.Sc.-B.Ed. First year students and the Office of Students 
helps in coordinating the course on Social Connect & Performing Arts/Sports in close association with the faculty 
advisors and students aims at helping the students in breaking the isolation, building connections with their peers, with 
the society and with the environment and practicing responsible connection through sustainability practices. This 
course comprises the 3 sub-courses: Social Connect/Excursion, Performing Arts, and Sports. In A.Y. 2024-25, a 
total of 554 students and 50 students were admitted in the UG (B.tech & B.S.) and B.Sc-B.Ed Ist year respectively. On 
08th March 2025, Around 604 new students along with 13 TAs, 26 Faculties and 13 Staff members from the Office of 
Students participated and coordinated the excursion. The places explored during the excursion were: Old City/
Heritage Walk (Jodhpur), Rao Jodha Park, Osian Temple and Mandore Garden. The students interacted with 
faculty, staff members and locals at the venue. It was a great learning experience for them.

List of activities done by Counselling Team, 
IIT Jodhpur in FY 2024-25
‘Nasha Mukt Bharat Pakhwada’ Event
Date: 20th June 2024
Aligned with the nationwide efforts to counter the spread of addiction, the Counselling Team of IIT Jodhpur organized an 
event as part of the “Nasha Mukt Bharat Pakhwada-2024, International Day against Drug Abuse and Illicit Trafficking”. It 
aimed to raise awareness and empower the IIT-J community to combat drug addiction and understand its harmful 
consequences.
The Honourable Director of IIT-J, Prof Avinash Kumar Agarwal and the Deputy Director, Prof. Sampat Raj Vadera addressed 
the audience.
The event featured presentations by Dr. Chandra Shekhar, Consultant Psychiatrist, Medipulse Hospital, Jodhpur; Mr. 
Hemant Jain, Advocate, Rajasthan High Court; and the Narcotics Control Bureau, Jodhpur represented by Mr. Dinesh 
Chauhan, Superintendent, and Mr. Sanjeev Kumar, Inspector. This was followed by administering a pledge to the audience 
for a Nasha-Mukt Bharat.
Formal Orientation
Date: 29th July- PG Students
Date: 30th July- UG Students
The formal orientation for the new batch of registrants was chaired by the esteemed Director of IIT Jodhpur and included 
other notable officials, such as the Dean of Academic Affairs and the Dean of Student Affairs. The event was further enriched 
by the presence of an honorary guest, Shri Gaurav Agrawal, Collector, who shared valuable insights and wisdom with the 
new students. The orientation covered a wide range of topics, including new teaching-learning initiatives, career progression 
and international opportunities, student life, and the overall campus experience. The program concluded with the Student 
Well-being Committee introducing various mental health facilities available on campus.
Delicate Discussions - on Menstrual Hygiene (female UG and PG students)
Date: 5th August 2024
To promote healthy and respectful campus living, basic knowledge of feminine hygiene is important for the new registrants, 
some of whom may be living in hostels for the first time. Accordingly, the M.O.-2 of IITJ, Dr. Neha Sharma, provided a 
detailed scientific presentation about menstruation, feminine care and healthy habits for individual and community 
cleanliness. The Q and A interaction was very successful.
Work-Life Balance: Perseverance and Acceptance
Date: 6th August 2024
Conducted by Mr. Akash Vishwakarma (Counsellor), this informal orientation session was focused on empowering students 
with the development of traits related to dealing with day-to-day life stressors. The session went successfully. It was an 
interactive session.
Aspects of Close Relationships
Date: 7th August 2024
An interactive session with the aim of understanding beliefs and behaviours about various close relationships, particularly 
family, friends and opposite-gender interests, was held in order to educate students about meaningful connections. Through 
storytelling and focussed group discussions, students came up with enlightening insights that showed well-reasoned and 
mature viewpoints. 
The session was conducted by Dr. Anjali Bhatia (Counsellor) and Ms. Nabeelah Siddiqui (Wellbeing Moderator).
Perfect Timing- Juggling Academic and Personal Priorities
Date: 8th August 2024
Time management is a basic life skill needed for students. This session, presented by Mr. Akash Vishwakarma, Counsellor, 
provided an opportunity to the students to understand the evidence-based approaches available to to adopt to manage their 
time and energy. The session was interactive.

PHC Services Introduction + Sleep Hygiene
Date: 9th August 2024
Presented by: Akash Vishwakarma, Counsellor; Medical Officer -1 Dr. Neha Sharma 
The orientation about the medical services is necessary information that everyone should have. Information about PHC was 
provided. Also, to provide solutions to sleep-related problems, a session on sleep hygiene was provided.
Social Things: Moving Towards A Peaceful Campus Life.
(Anti-Ragging Event + YourDost Orientation)
Date: 13th August 2024
Presented by: Ms. Priyanka Manchanda, Organizational Psychologist, YourDost In observance of UGC’s Anti-Ragging Week 
from 12 to 18 August, the SWC organized an orientation session to educate and empower the first-year students against 
ragging. Ms. Priyanka Manchanda from YourDost, IIT-J’s online counselling service, conducted this event. Through 
interactive skill-building activities, she educated the students about conflict-resolution and respectful community living in a 
residential campus.
Posters and information about the Anti-Ragging guidelines of the UGC were prominently displayed in and around the 
venue, and at various locations around the campus. The session saw packed attendance and lively participation by the 
students. 
 
Gravity of the Matter: PoSH Awareness for SWC Members
Date: 28th August 2024
Presented by: Ms. Preeti Badola, Assistant Professor, National Law University Jodhpur
Wardens, Counsellors, and Student Guides tend to be amongst the first people in whom a campus resident may confide. 
Therefore, they need to understand the legal framework of what constitutes sexual harassment. An expert view on this was 
provided by Ms. Preeti Badola by explaining the prevailing laws and guidelines on this issue. This was followed by an 
interactive session where the audience had many of their questions answered.
Using Theatre Techniques for Developing Awareness
Date: 2nd September 2024
Conducted by: Ms.Suhasini Seelin- Adjunct faculty SoLA
To enhance the effectiveness in mentoring and improve interaction with mentees, a theatre-based workshop was conducted 
for UG student guides to improve their self-awareness and approachability.
This 1.5-hour session led by Ms. Suhasini, involved around 20 participants in activities designed to explore the connection 
between breath and voice, body posture, and the physical expression of emotions.
World Suicide Prevention Day: 10th September 2024 - Signature Campaign
On 10th September 2024, World Suicide Prevention Day, the Indian Institute of Technology Jodhpur (IITJ) organized an 
awareness program by conducting a signature campaign at different venues inside the campus. This event aimed to 
encourage open conversations about suicide and the mental health challenges contributing to it. Students, faculty, and staff 
participated enthusiastically in signing the pledge to prioritize mental health.
Prof. Sampat Raj Vadera, Distinguished Professor; Prof. Ankita Sharma, Dean of Students Affairs (DOSA); and Mr Akash 
Vishwakarma (Clinical Psychologist), Counsellor at IIT Jodhpur, addressed the gathering about the importance of proactive 
mental health measures.
PoSH Awareness for First Year PG students
Date: 11th September, 2024
Presented by: Ms. Preeti Badola, Assistant Professor, National Law University Jodhpur In continuation of the efforts to 
educate the campus community about the PoSH Act and the guidelines for appropriate behaviour in IITJ, Ms. Preeti Badola 
conducted an engaging session peppered with relatable examples for first-year PG students. Members of the PG student 
team, and the counselling team were present to provide depth to the discussion. The interaction which followed the session 
indicated their receptivity towards the precise presentation of legal guidelines.
A Classroom of Insights: Introduction to Counselling Services for ITEP First Batch
Date: 19th September 2024
Audience: first batch of ITEP (B.Sc.-B.Ed.) in CETE
The Counselling Team organized an awareness program aimed at fostering a balanced approach to student life. The event 
featured an interactive discussion on essential life skills, led by Akash Vishwakarma. The second session, conducted by Dr.

Dr.Anjali Bhatia, focused on helping students understand their individual strengths and weaknesses. The program 
concluded with a meditation exercise, leaving all the new students appreciative of the valuable insights shared throughout 
the event.
World Mental Health Day Activity: All-Time Mindful sessions
Date: 14th to 18th October 2024
Every year, the World Mental Health Day is celebrated on the 10th of October. The theme for 2024 was “Mental Health at 
Work" -- (World Health Organization). The Counselling Team organized events through which the campus community could 
participate in rejuvenating and mindful activities. 
Dr. Anjali Bhatia, Counsellor, conducted short, guided mindfulness sessions for 5 days. The aim of this activity was to foster 
a daily habit of sitting with concentrated and relaxed attention.
World Mental Health Day Activity: Recharge Zone
Date: 18th October 2024
The Recharge Zone event facilitated by Ms. Nabeelah Siddiqui was a vibrant and engaging initiative aimed at providing 
students with a break from their academic routines. The focus was to provide a stress buster and help students find joy 
through mindful indulgence in art.
The event featured various stress-busting and relaxing activities, including a "Worry Jar" where students could let go of 
their worries, a "Caught Being Kind" board to promote positive reflections and gratitude, a collaborative art 
mural that encouraged creativity, joy and social connections, and a clay and slime corner.
World Meditation Day
Date: 21st December 2024
Conducted by: Mr. Siddhanth Chaturbhuj (Ph.D. Student) a Yoga and Meditation teacher
On the occasion of the first World Meditation Day, the Counselling Team organized a serene and transformative meditation 
session, open to all members of the campus community (above 13 years of age).
Wellness Circles, Second Edition
Date: March 2025 onwards
Facilitated by : Dr. Anjali Bhatia (Counsellor), Ms. Nabeelah Siddiqui, Mr. Sahib Kumar Sunani, Mr. Sachin Kumar Nanda, 
Ms. Elizabeth Wilson (Junior Counsellors)
The Wellness Circles are focussed groups for long-term, regular activities that promote different aspects of psychological 
well-being. Each group has a specific theme, facilitated by a Counsellor or Junior Counsellor. These circles are held at regular 
intervals (for 45-60 minute sessions) to learn various skills, share experiences, or simply de-stress.
The Circles running in the current academic cycle are -- Enwision: Guided Imagery for Insight, Creativity and Connection ; 
Inner Canvas; First-Aid to Rejection; Manopravad: Freedom, Responsibility and Choices; and Boosting PsyCap: Unlocking 
the Inner Hero.
Review Talk on Psychological Wellbeing (Department of Physics)
Date: 9 April, 2025
As invited by the Head of the Department of Physics, Dr. Anjali Bhatia (Counsellor) conducted a review talk on academic and 
career challenges with reference to psychological wellbeing.
Using this platform to walk the students through the counselling process, the SWC support network and the counselling team 
in particular, Dr. Anjali also covered aspects such as preventive mental hygiene, healthy habits, respectful community living, 
establishing boundaries, setting priorities, and time management.

Ambedkar Jayanti: Date: 16 April 2024
Description: As part of the Ambedkar Jayanti celebrations held on 16 April 2024, an essay writing competition was 
organized to honour the legacy and contributions of Dr. B.R. Ambedkar, particularly in the fields of constitutional 
development and social justice in India. The event aimed to promote awareness and inspire students to reflect on his 
ideals and vision. A notable achievement during the event was the participation of EBSB (Ek Bharat Shreshtha Bharat) 
members. One of the EBSB members secured a prize in the Hindi essay writing competition, showcasing both literary skill 
and a deep understanding of Dr. Ambedkar’s philosophies. This activity served as a meaningful engagement for students, 
reinforcing the values of equality, justice, and national integration.
Independence Day: Date:15th August 2024
Description: As part of the 77th Independence Day celebrations at IIT Jodhpur on 15th August 2024, the EBSB student 
team made a special contribution by performing a soulful patriotic group song. Their melodious rendition beautifully 
captured the spirit of unity, cultural pride, and love for the nation. The heartfelt performance resonated deeply with the 
audience, adding an emotional and inspiring dimension to the event. Through their voices, the EBSB team paid a musical 
tribute to the sacrifices of the freedom fighters and celebrated the essence of India’s unity in diversity.
National Unity Day: Date: 28 October 2024
Description: On the occasion of National Unity Day, celebrated to commemorate the birth anniversary of Sardar 
Vallabhbhai Patel, a painting activity was organized on 28 October 2024. The event aimed to highlight the values of unity, 
integrity, and cultural diversity in India. EBSB members actively participated by preparing paintings depicting the life 
and contributions of Sardar Patel, as well as showcasing the diverse art forms from different regions of India. The artwork 
reflected the spirit of national integration and celebrated India’s rich cultural heritage. This creative initiative encouraged 
students to express their patriotism and appreciation for unity in diversity through art.
Essay and Poetry Competitions on Bhagwan Birsa Munda Jayanti (Jan Jatiya Gaurav Diwas): Date: 
20 November 2024
Description: To commemorate the 150th birth anniversary of Bhagwan Birsa Munda on Jan Jatiya Gaurav Diwas 2024, a 
series of engaging literary activities were organized to honour the legacy of the great tribal freedom fighter and 
acknowledge the invaluable contributions of indigenous communities to India’s freedom struggle.
Two competitions were conducted as part of the celebration:
Essay Writing Competition on the topic “Impact of Indigenous Tribes on Today’s India”
Poetry Competition themed “India’s Indigenous Peoples: Pioneers of the Freedom Movement”
These events witnessed enthusiastic participation from students, faculty, staff, children, and campus residents. The 
initiative provided a platform for all participants to express their thoughts, showcase their creativity, and reflect on the 
cultural and historical significance of India’s tribal heritage.
The EBSB team played an active role in organizing and promoting the event, reinforcing the spirit of national pride and 
unity in diversity. We extend our heartfelt gratitude to all participants for their insightful contributions and for making 
the event a memorable tribute to Bhagwan Birsa Munda.
